- 57-            ANNEX 1
ANNEX 1: BACKGROUND TO HUBEI PROVINCE AND
PROJECT CITIES
Hubei Province
I.    Hubei Province is located in Central China and is bordered clockwise from the north
by the Provinces of Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Sichuan and Shaanxi. It is traversed by
the mid-reaches of the Changjiang (Yangtze) River, the largest in the country. The
Province has a total land area of 186,000 km2 and a population of 55 million (1990), of
which about 15 million (27 percent) live in urban areas. While total population in the
Province has been growing at about 1.4 percent, nonagricultural population growth has been
about 8 percent a year since 1980. It ranks ninth among Chinese provinces and autonomous
regions in terms of population and aggregate GNP (Y 100 billion in 1992), and fourteenth
in terms of GNP per capita (Y 1,460).
2.    The topography of the Province is mountainous and hilly, except in the south. It has
a subtropical, hurnid, monsoonal climate with hot wet summers and dry winters. The
Province is prone to frequent droughts and floods. The average annual rainfall is 750 to
1.500 mm (30 to 59 inches). Although still predominately a rural province, industry
accounts for two thirds of Hubei's gross domestic output value, mainly from state-owned
enterprises that employ about two thirds of the industrial work force, mostly in heavy
industries, notably iron, steel, cement and chemicals.
luangshi
3.    Huangshi is located in the southeastem part of Hubei Province, on the south bank of
the middle reaches of the Changjiang (Yangtze) River and north of Huangjing Mountain,
and is the second largest city of the Province. Cihu, Daye and Quinshan Lakes lie in its
hinterland. There are four urban districts (Huangshigang, Shihuiyao, Xialu and Tieshan)
and one suburban county (Daye) in the city.
4.    The total municipal area is about 1,850 km2, of which the urban area is just under
10 percent. The total population is 1.35 million, of which the urban population is 510,000.
The 1-rban population density is around 3,000 persons per kmi2; the urban population is
expected to reach about 660,000 by year 2010.
5.    Historically, Huangshi was famous for its ore smelting. With the Daye steel plant,
an iron mine, a coal mine and a cement plant, it was among the pioneers of modem industry
in China. From this background, the city has developed an industrial base with a full range
of activities covering metallurgy, machinery, power generation, building materials and



- 58 -            ANNEX 1
textiles. The industrial output value was Y 3.3 billion in 1990; this is expected to reach
around Y 6.6 billion by year 2000.
6.    About 90 percent of the urban area in the vicinity of Shenyanggang Canal is served
by a piped combined wastewater and stormwater drainage system. A recently com3leted
secondary wastewater treatment plant in Huangshigang, with a capacity of 20,000 m /day,
is currently treating a mix of 70 percent industrial and 30 percent domestic wastewater. The
plant is operating at about 70 percent capacity. However, construction work is underway to
divert flows presently entering the northeast corner of Cihu Lake, to this treatment plant.
Untreated industrial effluent is currently being discharged into the southern area of Cihu
Lake, resulting in significant deterioration of the natural water quality and associated loss of
amenity to local residents. A major objective of the Huangshi Wastewater component is to
improve the water quality of Cihu Lake.
7.    The problems of solid waste and nightsoil management in Huangshi are typical of
those in Wuhan, Xiangfan and Yichang. While the primary collection systems are
effective, problems arise in the transfer, transport and disposal of the wastes. The handling
and uncontrolled disposal of wastes, often at illegal sites, pose health hazards to sanitation
department workers in particular, and to the public in general. Nightsoil is often applied
directly to fields before being allowed to digest in storage tanks. The major objectives of
the project cities' solid waste and nightsoil management components are, therefore, to
improve transfer facilities, transportation, and the ultimate disposal of wastes in an
environmentally acceptable manner.
Wuhan
8.    Wuhan is located in the east of Hubei Province in Central China and is the
Provincial capital. The Yangtze River enters the city from the southwest and the Han River
joins the Yangtze coming from the west. The two rivers divide the city into three parts:
Hankou, Wuchang and Hanyang. The city has seven urban districts (Jiangan, Jianhang,
Qiaokou, Hangyan, Wuchang, Quingshan and Hongshan), two suburban districts
(Dongxihu and Hannan) and four suburban counties (Wuchang, Huangpi, Hanyang and
Xinzhou). The area is generally flat with a large number of lakes. The highest point of the
city is Yujia Hill, 152 meters above sea level.
9.    The total municipal area is some 8,500 km2, of which the urban area is
approximately 10percent. The 1992 population of the municipality was about 6.8
million, of which the urban population was estimated to be 3.5 million. The urban
population density in the city is around 4,000 persons per km 2; the urban population is
expected to reach some 7.65 million by year 2000.
10.   Wuhan is a regional transportation center, located at the mid-point of the major
north-south rail line linking Beijing to Guangzhou. The Yangtze River is dredged to
provide a transportation route from Shanghai to Sichuan Province.



- 59 -           ANNEX 1
11.  In Wuhan there are some 4,500 industrial enterprises, making the city one of the
most important industrial centers in China. The main industries are iron and steel,
chemical, electronics, machinery and weaving. Wuhan Iron and Steel Works is one of the
largest in China, producing 7 million tons annually. The total industrial output was Y 22
billion in 1992, this is expected to increase tenfold by year 2010.
12.   About 60 percent of the urban area is served by a piped combined stormwater and
wastewater drainage system. Over 90 percent of the urban population is served by septic
tanks, with the effluent discharging to the combined system and open ditches. The
remaining population is served by water flush and dry pit communal public latrines.
13.   There are about 10 wastewater outfalls discharging directly into East Lake, which
is an existing source of municipal water supply. A further outfall, which accounted for
about 50 percent of the wastewater flows entering East lake, has now been diverted to the
Changjiang River.  A recently completed secondary wastewater treatment plant at
Waishahu, with a design capacity of 50,000 m3/d, was shut down a few weeks after
commissioning for lack of operating funds. One of the major objective of the Wuhan
Wastewater component is to improve the quality of the water body in East Lake.
Xiangfan
14.   Xiangfan, located in the northwestern part of Hubei Province, is a hub in the area
of four Provinces: Hubei, Henan, Sichuan and Shanxi. The city is divided in two
sections (Fancheng and Xiangyang) by the Han River, the largest tributary of the
Changjiang River, entering the city from the west. There are four urban districts
(Xiangcheng, Fandong, Fanxi and Jiaoqu) and two development zones (Xiangfan
Automobile Industry Zone and Fandong New Hi-Tech Zone). The area of Xiangfan is
generally flat.
15.   The total municipal area and population are 326 km and 584,000, respectively, of
which the urban area and population are 40 km2 and 475,000, respectively. The urban
2
population density is just under 12,000 persons per km .
16.   More than 80 percent of the existing urban area are served by a combined storm
and wastewater system. Over 80 percent of the population are served by septic tanks.
Fancheng, on the north side of the Han River, is divided into five drainage areas, three of
which discharge mainly domestic waste directly into the Han River. The remaining two
areas, Quinghekou and Qilihe, discharge predominantly industrial waste to the Qili and
Xiaoqing Rivers, which drain into the Han River. The Qili and Xiaoqing Rivers are
highly polluted.
17.   Xiangcheng, on the south side of the Han River, has three drainage systems, two
of which discharge to the river. The third system, in the old city area, discharges into the
city moat, which has, as a result, become highly polluted.



- 60 -           ANNEX 1
18.   There are two industrial wastewater treatment plants in Xiangfan, each of
10,000 m3/d capacity. Both plants are owned by textile factories, but operated by the
Xiangfan Environmental Protection Bureau.  Effluent from these plants, which is
understood to comply with Chinese national standards, is discharged to the Qili River.
19.   Planned development to the north and west of Fancheng will add further waste
loads to Qili River. A major objective of the project, therefore, is to address water quality
in this river, as well as Xiaoqing River and the city moat.
Yichang
20.   Yichang is located in the westem part of Hubei Province on the middle-upper
reaches of Changjiang River and is the location of the Three Gorges Dam and Ge7houba
Hydraulic Conservancy Project. The city is divided into two parts by the Changjiang
River and has three urban districts, Xiling, Wujia and Dianjun. The urban area is long
and narrow and the region is hilly, between mountainous land and the plains.
21.   The total municipal area is about 33 kin2, with the urban area covering 29 kM2, or
about 88 percent of total area. The total population is approximately 479,000, of whom
391,000 are classified as urban. The population density in the urban area is 13,000
persons per km .
22.   Yichang is a major Chinese scenic area and also the country's largest Hydraulic
Conservancy location. Tourism will gain increasing importance with the construction of
the Three Gorges Dam. The main industries are power generation, machinery, textile,
electronics, metallurgical and various light industries.
23.   The existing urban area is served by a combined storm and wastewater system,
except for new development areas (e.g., Dongshan Economic Development Zone), where
separate sewerage and drainage systems are being constructed.  Wastes from this
development zone are presently being discharged to the Yuen River, with the possibility
of compromising the city's No. I water supply intake. Waste discharges from elsewhere
in the city to the Changjiang River could compromise the No. 2 water supply intake. The
objective of Yichang's Wastewater component would be to collect effluent for discharge
into the Changjiang downstream from the existing intakes.



- 61-                      ANNEX2
ANNEX 2: DETAILED PROJECT DESCRIPTION
I.    The components of the proposed project investments are described in detail below
and summarized in tabular form.
A. HUANGSHI
Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
2.    Huangshi City includes a number of scenic lakes, of which the largest freshwater
lakes are Cihu Lake with a total surface area of approximately 8.4 km2 and Daye Lake
about 12 km south of the central urban area with a total surface area of approximately
57 km2. The present total wastewater flow of the city is about 500,000 m3/d, consisting of
29 percent domestic and 71 percent industrial flows. Cihu Lake carries about 150,000 m3/d
(30 percent) of the total urban wastewater, and the south arm is severely polluted, mainly by
industrial wastes. The existing wastewater treatment plant at Huangshigang deals with
about 20,000 m3/d from the Huangshigang catchment. The wastewater flow in 2010 is
estimated at about 510,000 m3/d. The proposed municipal wastewater master plan for
Huangshi urban area for year 2010 includes construction of a major wastewater collection
and treatment facility to be built at Chenjiawan to deal with the waste flows from
Shenyanggang, Chenjiawan, Tuanchenshan and Lao Xialu areas. Small systems would be
built to cover the separate Huahu and Xizai catchments; all these wastewater systems would
discharge into the Yangtze River. The Master Plan proposes that the wastewater from the
separate minor catchments of Tieshan, Xialu and Shannan would be treated separately
before being discharged southward to the Daye Lake.
3.    The Hluangshi wastewater component is designed to address the pollution of Cihu
Lake, which is a shallow lake located immediately adjacent to the principal urban area and
central business district of Huangshi and is an attractive shoreline readily accessible to large
numbers of urban dwellers. Its beneficial uses are passive recreation, swimming, fishing
and boating. At present, the lake receives substantial quantities of untreated domestic
sewage and industrial wastewater, and is significantly polluted; also, the excessive
concentrations of nitrogen and phosphorus in the water have accelerated the rate of
eutrophication and the natural water quality has been progressively degraded.
4.    The Chenjiwan wastewater system, which is the first priority component of
Huangshi's master plan, provides for the collection, treatment, and disposal of municipal
wastewater currently discharged to Cihu Lake. This wastewater system includes three trunk
sewers collecting municipal wastewater from the northern, central and southern sections of
the catchmnent area; with preliminary treatment, prior to discharge to the Yangtze River via



- 62 -                     ANNEX2
the existing Shanyanggang canal, thus preventing the continued discharge of untreated
municipal wastewater to Cihu Lake. The effective management of further nutrient addition
to the lake would reduce the rate of eutrophication, thereby improving the water quality in
the Lake to enhance the amenity, recreational and land use values of surrounding areas.
Due to financial constraints, only the first phase of the system, comprising the southem
interceptor and preliminary treatment would be implemented under the project.
5.    Proposed Component ($11.9 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Chenjianwan Southern Trunks and Interceptors including about 6 km of
sewers ranging in size from about 1,200 to 1,500 mm diameter. Miaopu and
Yegang pump stations of about 68,000 and 96,000 m3/d capacity, and force
mains of about 1,000 mm diameter.
(b)   Southern Collection Sewers including about 9 km of sewers ranging from
about 400 to 800 mm diameter to discharge to southem trunk sewers.
(c)   Chenjianwan  Preliminary  Treatment Plant and  Pump  Station
comprising screens, grit removal facilities, pumping equipment of about
160,000 m3/d capacity, and 1.1 km delivery main of about 1,600 mm
diameter to discharge treated effluent to the Shanyanggang canal.
Municipal Wastes Management
6.    The objective of this component is to improve the primary collection system by the
construction of small transfer stations, provision of additional trucks for transport of solid
waste from transfer stations to landfill and the replacement of open collection trucks by
larger closed compactor vehicles for areas where waste is picked up from collection points
for direct delivery to landfill.  For final disposal, the first stage of a move from
semicontrolled landfill to fully controlled landfill operation meeting state-approved
standards will be taken by the provision of a new landfill at Xisai. To improve nightsoil
and sludge collection, vacuum trucks will be provided.
7.    The new landfill will be controlled and operated by the Huangshi City Appearance
and Environmental Sanitation Bureau (HCA&ESB), which is responsible to the Huangshi
Urban Construction Commission (HUCC) for the management of municipal solid waste
and nightsoil collection and disposal. The urban district environmental sanitation bureaus
(ESBs) of Huangshi, Shihuiyao, Xialu and Tieshan will continue to be responsible for
providing municipal solid waste and nightsoil collection services and street sweeping.
Industrial and commercial enterprises and institutions will retain the responsibility for
transportation and disposal of their own wastes, but may request the ESBs to provide these
services on payment of the appropriate service fees.



- 63 -                      ANNEX2
8.    Proposed Component ($4.5 million). The component would comprise:
(a)    Transfer Stations: construction of 10 small mechanical-loading transfer
stations to accept municipal solid waste from hand carts and small collection
vehicles for transfer to large trucks for transportation to final disposal sites.
Design capacity of the stations will be in the order of 50 tons to 100 tons per
day (tpd), related to the waste generation area to be served. Sites have
already been identified on land owned by the city government.
(b)    Collection  Vehicles:  (i) for solid waste collection and disposal:
procurement of four compactor collection vehicles with a carrying capacity
of approximately 8 tons for direct delivery of municipal solid waste from
collection points to landfill, 12 5-ton capacity trucks for secondary
transportation of waste from  transfer stations and  20 0.5-ton small
collection trucks to provide primary collection services in selected areas
with restricted access; and (ii) for nightsoil and sludge collection and
disposal: procurement of 12 vacuum trucks.
(c)    Sanitary Landfill:  site preparation works and construction of a new
sanitary landfill to national standards at a 12.4 ha site of mainly derelict land
at Xisai, adjoining a large chemical plant. The valley site has a volume of
some 1.25 million m 3 and, with the proposed design capacity of around
150 tpd rising to 300 tpd, would have an estimated life of at least 15 years.
The preliminary design includes provision of gas and leachate treatment
systems, site offices, weighbridge, maintenance and labor facilities, a 5 m-
wide all-weather access road of some 1.2 km, a steel-wheeled compactor for
consolidation of the waste, and two small bulldozers, three 5-ton dump
trucks for moving and spreading covering material.
(d)   Institutional Development and Training: provision will be made for
institutional development and practical training of both management and
operational personnel, with particular attention being given to the control,
management and monitoring necessary to effectively operate a sanitary
landfill.
B. WUHAN
Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
9.    Wuhan Wuchang Central Wastewater System. The Wuhan Wuchang central
wastewater component is designed to address the pollution of the East Lake, which is the
source of drinking water for the population of the lake area, and with banks extending over
111.5 km, is one of the most important scenic attractions in Wuhan. It is also used for
recreational purposes and fish farming, as well as being the site for research on aquatic
ecology. The lake has been receiving substantial quantities of municipal and industrial
wastewater for many years, currently estimated at 180,000 m3/d. The lake is significantly



- 64 -                     ANNEX2
polluted and has thick deposits of sludge on the bottom, which contains high concentrations
of heavy metals, nutrients and other contamninants.
10.   The component provides for the collection, treatment, and disposal of municipal
wastewater currently discharged to the lake, and, in Stage I, provides for the interception of
all wastewater and primary treatment augmentation at the existing Shahu plant, new
Erlangmiao and Longwanzui wastewater collection and primary treatment facilities.
Effluents from the facilities flow, respectively, to the Luojiagang Canal for discharge to the
Yangtze River and to Nanhu Lake to significantly improve water quality in the Lake to
facilitate the continued use of the resource for municipal water supply and to enhance
amenity value. Municipal service delivery would be improved for about 0.9 million
persons presently living in the catchment area. In order to prevent drawdown of the water
level in East Lake, water balance facilities from the Yangtze River would be provided.
11.   Hankou Wastewater System.  The Hankou wastewater system provides for
additional wastewater collection and preliminary treatmnent facilities in West Hankou, with
effluent discharge to the Fu River, to improve the standard of municipal services for this
major center of population currently experiencing rapid urban development. Risks to public
health would be reduced and the standard of amenity improved in a densely populated
urban area, thus benefiting some 800,000 persons.
12.   Hanyang Wastewater System. Wastewater from the predominantly industrial area
of Hanyang is presently discharged untreated into the Moshui Lake, where water quality is
poor (below Class V Chinese Standard). This shallow lake provides beneficial uses
including fish farming, and important recreational facilities at the adjacent zoological
gardens. The Hanyang system would provide wastewater collection, preliminary treatment
and effluent disposal facilities, improving the Moshui Lake beneficial use and providing
improved municipal service to some 200,000 inhabitants in the Nantaizihu Lake catchment.
13.   Proposed Component ($124.5 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
Wuchang System
(a)   Shahu Wastewater System including the construction of about 16 km of
300 to 1,200 mm diameter sewers, pump stations, and Shahu primary
treatment plant, extending the treatment capacity from 50,000 currently to
I 00,000 m3/d.
(b)   Erlangmiao Wastewater System  including the construction of about
16 km of sewers of 300 to 2,000 mm diameter, and culverts, and Erlangmiao
primary treatment plant and facilities of about 180,000 m3/d capacity.
(c)   Effluent Discharge Culvert for Shahu and Erlangmiao  systems,
comprising about 4.3 km of pipes and culverts, together with effluent
discharge arrangements.



- 65 -                     ANNEX2
(d)   Longwangzui Wastewater System including the construction of about
32 km of sewers, and force mains, in sizes about 300 to 1,800 mm diameter,
and several pump stations of about 160,000 m3/d total capacity.
(e)   Longwangzui Wastewater Treatment Plant comprising primary treatmcnt
and associated sludge facilities of about 150,000 m3/d capacity, together
with effluent discharge arrangements.
(f)    East Lake Water Balance System comprising a floating pump station on
Yangtze River of about 200,000 m3/d capacity, force main, control gates,
sedimentation facilities on Luojia Canal, and outlet to East Lake.
Hankou System
(g)   Hankou West Wastewater System comprising about 6 km of culverts of
reinforced concrete and brick, or other construction material, in sizes in the
range 1.8 m x 1.5 m high to 4.2 m x 2.2 m high; about 10 km of connecting
sewers, in sizes between 300 to 1,000 in diameter; about 7.5 km of open-
channel construction with control gates, pump station and preliminary
treatment plant of about 400,000 m3/d capacity, and effluent discharge
channel to Fu River.
Hanyang System
(h)   Nantaizihu Wastewater System comprising about 6 km of sewers of sizes
300 to 1,800 mm diameter and culverts of reinforced concrete and brick
construction in sizes in the range 2.0 m x 1.7 m high to 3.8 m x 2.5 m high,
pump station and preliminary treatment plant at Nantaizihu of about
100,000 m3/d capacity, effluent discharge main, outfall pump station of
capacity about 100,000 m3/d, and outfall to Yangtze River.
Municipal Wastes Management
14.   The objective of this component is to improve the primary collection system by the
provision of large capacity compactor vehicles for business, commercial and modem
residential areas where wastes can be picked up from collection points for direct delivery to
landfill. For final disposal, an existing semicontrolled landfill at Jinkou will be extended.
The existing area will be upgraded where possible and the extended area will be operated to
national standards.
15.   The landfill will be controlled and operated by the Wuhan Environmental Sanitation
Bureau (WESB), which is responsible to the Wuhan Urban Construction Commission
(WUCC) for the management of municipal solid waste and nightsoil collection and
disposal. The city's seven urban district ESBs will continue to be responsible for providing
municipal solid waste and nightsoil collection services and street sweeping, under the
guidance and supervision of WESSB. Industrial and commercial enterprises and institutionrs



- 66 -                      ANNEX2
will retain the responsibility for transportation and disposal of their own wastes but may
request the ESBs to provide these services on payment of the appropriate service fees.
16.   Proposed Component ($18.0 million). The proposed component is as follows:
(a)   Collection Vehicles: procurement of about 30 closed-compactor collection
vehicles with a can-ying capacity of approximately 8 tons for direct delivery
of wastes from collection points to landfill.
(b)   Sanitary Landfill: site preparation works, construction and upgrading of
an existing landfill to national standards by extending the site area by
40.0 ha, with the possibility of a further future extension to 93.3 ha. With a
total volume of 8.5 million m3, the proposed daily input rising from the
present 750 tpd to 2,000 tpd would give an estimated life of some 15 years.
The preliminary design includes provision of gas and leachate treatment
systems, site offices, weighbridge, maintenance and labor facilities.
Proposed equipment includes two steel-wheeled compactors for
consolidation of the waste, two tracked excavators, four bulldozers, three
loading shovels, six 5-ton dump trucks for excavating, moving and
spreading covering material, one car, and, for site supervision and general
duties, one pickup truck and a personnel carrier.
(c)   Institutional Development and Training: provision will be made for
institutional development and practical training of both management and
operational personnel, with particular attention being given to the control,
management and monitoring necessary to effectively operate a sanitary
landtill.
C. XIANGFAN
Wastewater Collection, Treatment and Disposal
17.   Xiangfan City is situated mainly on the banks of the Han River with some
development spreading up the Tangbai, Xiaoqing and Qili Rivers. The central urban
districts are divided by the Han River into the southern, mainly residential and old town
area of Xiangcheng and the northern, predominantly industrial and commercial area of
Fancheng. Wastewater from five combined sewer systems in Fancheng is discharged
directly to the Han River through six outlets along the left bank of the River and via the Qili
and Xiaoqing Rivers. Sewerage from three drainage systems in Xiangcheng is discharged
to the old moat and Nanqu ditch and ultimately to the Han River. The present urban
wastewater flow is around 500,000 m3/d, comprising about 40 percent domestic flow and
60 percent from industrial sources. Three existing treatment plants, with a combined
capacity of about 40,000 m3/d, are located in Fancheng and Youfanfgang (20,000 m3/d).
The average wastewater flow in 2010 is projected around 1,000,000 m /d.



- 67 -                     ANNEX2
18.   The Xiangfan Wastewater Master Plan includes the proposed Xiangfan central
urban wastewater system, which covers the areas of Fancheng and Xiangfen. This proposed
scheme would intercept the wastewater from the existing combined sewers in these areas,
provide collector systems discharging to a treatment facility to be established on
Yuliangzhou Island, which is located on the east side of the Han River. The master plan
proposes that wastewater from the outlying areas of Youfanggang, Zhangwan, Dongjin and
Yujiahu would be provided with separate collection and treatment systems to intercept
municipal wastewater flows, which presently discharge to the Han, Qili, and Xiaoqing
Rivers; the Moat and Nanqu ditch.
19.   The objective of this component, which is the first phase of an integrated program,
is to provide improved municipal services and environmental conditions for about 250,000
persons in the most densely populated (Fancheng) area of the city, through effective
wastewater interception, treatment and disposal. The component would significantly reduce
pollution of the Xiaoqing and Qilihe Rivers, thereby reducing the risk of contamination of
water supply intakes located on the Han River.
20.   Proposed Component ($48.0 million). The proposed component would comprise
the following works:
(a)   Fancheng Interceptor and Sewer System comprising about 14 km of
trunk sewers ranging in size from 600 to 2,000 mm diameter, about 6 km of
culvert in sizes between 1.4 m x 1.2 m high and 3.2 m x 2.0 m high, pump
station of about 525,000 m3/d capacity, access bridge across Han River to
Yuliangzhou Island, and about 3 km of 2,200 mm diameter force main.
(b)   Yuliangzhou Preliminary Treatment Plant comprising screening, grit
removal facilities of about 600,000 m3/d capacity, and outfall of about
1,800 mm diameter to Han River.
Municipal Wastes Management
21.   The objectives of this component are to improve the efficiency and environmental
standards of waste collection and disposal. To help achieve this, 16 transfer stations will be
constructed. The first phase of a new landfill will be constructed at a site yet to be finalized,
in the northem area of the city to supplement the present semicontrolled landfill at
Huoshishan in the south. The new landfill will be designed and operated to approved
national standards.
22.   The landfill will be controlled and operated by the Xiangfan Environmental
Sanitation Department (XESD), which is responsible to the Xiangfan Urban Construction
Commission (XUCC) for the management of municipal solid waste and nightsoil collection
and disposal. The city's three urban district ESBs will continue to be responsible for
providing these services and street sweeping, under the guidance and supervision of XESD.
Industrial and commercial enterprises and institutions will retain the responsibility for



- 68 -                      ANNEX2
transportation and disposal of their own wastes, but may request the ESBs to provide these
services on payment of the appropriate service fees.
23.   Proposed Component ($5.4 million). The proposed solid waste management
component is as follows:
(a)    Sanitary Landfill: site preparation works and construction a new landfill to
national standards at a site north of the city. The preliminary design
standards include provision of gas and leachate treatment systems, site
offices, weighbridge, site and vehicle maintenance and labor facilities and an
all-weather access road. For site operations, one steel-wheeled compactor
for consolidation of the wastes, one bulldozer, one loading shovel, and three
5-ton dump trucks for excavating and spreading will be provided, together
with one car, one pickup truck and one personnel carrier for supervision and
general duties.
(b)   Transfer Stations: Construction of about 16 transfer stations.
(c)    Collection Vehicles: Procurement of about 45 collection vehicles.
(d)   Institutional Development and Training: provision will be made for
institutional development and practical training of both management and
operational personnel, with particular attention being given to the control,
management and monitoring necessary to effectively operate a sanitary
landfill.
1). YICHANG
Municipal Wastes Management
24.   The objectives of this component are to improve the efficiency and environmental
standards of waste disposal. In addition to nightsoil and sludge collection upgrading, the
first phase of a new landfill will be constructed at Huangjiawan, in the north of the city, to
supplement the present semicontrolled landfill at Ganxigou in the central area. The new
landfill will be designed and operated to national standards.
25.   The landfill will be controlled and operated by the Yichang Environmental
Sanitation Department (YESD), which is responsible to the Yichang Urban Construction
Commission (YUCC) for the management of municipal solid waste and nightsoil collection
and disposal. The city's three urban district ESDs will continue to be responsible for
providing these services and street sweeping, under the guidance and supervision of YESD.
Industrial and commercial enterprises and institutions will retain responsibility for the
transportation and disposal of their own wastes, but may request the ESDs to provide these
services on payment of the appropriate service fees.



- 69 -                      ANNEX2
26.   Proposed Component ($9.1 million). The proposed component is as follows:
(a)   Sanitary Landfill:  site preparation works and construction of a new
landfill to national standards at Huangjiawan, some 8 km from the city
center. The site has a surface area of some 20.0 ha and a volume of
2.8 million m3. At the proposed design capacity of 420 tpd rising to 500 tpd,
this would give an estimated life of some 15 years. The preliminary design
includes provision of gas and leachate treatment and monitoring systems,
site offices, weighbridge, maintenance and labor facilities and a 2.5 km all-
weather access road. For site operations, one steel-wheeled compactor for
consolidation of the waste, one bulldozer, one loading shovel and three 5-ton
dump trucks for excavating and spreading cover will be provided, together
with one 4-four-wheel-drive jeep and one personnel carrier for supervision
and general duties.
(b)   Vacuum Trucks for Nightsoil and Sludge Collection: purchase of five
trucks
(c)   Institutional Development and Training: provision will be made for
institutional development and practical training of both management and
operational personnel, with particular attention being given to the control,
management and monitoring necessary to effectively operate a sanitary
landfill.
E. INDUSTRIAL POLLUTION CONTROL SUBPROJECTS
27.   The industrial pollution control subprojects have been designed to achieve both
pollution reduction and improvements in operational efficiency through structural
transformation to efficient and low polluting technologies, waste minimization/reuse and, as
appropriate, product upgrading. The component would assist targeted large-scale industrial
enterprises to bring their effluent discharge to comply with national, or local, standards in a
cost-effective manner.
28.   A pipeline of large-scale projects, amounting to about $50 million of subloans, has
been screened by the Bank/IDA and certified by the local EPBs as requiring immediate
cleanup measures. A line-of-credit of $45 million would be provided under the proposed
Bank Loan/IDA Credit to help finance the subloans. The proposed Bank/IDA-financed
subloan for each subproject would be limited to 100 percent of foreign exchange c -sts, or
50 percent of total subproject costs, whichever is higher.
29.   Subproject Appraisal Arrangements.  The environmental/technical appraisal
would include (a) an assessment of the subproject's consistency with the municipal
environmental strategy and its priority; (b) the impact of the proposed subproject on
pollution prevention and reduction; and (c) compliance with national/local environmental
regulations. The economic appraisal would have to demonstrate that (a) all feasible options
for pollution reduction have been examined and that the solution proposed is the most cost-



- 70 -                     ANNEX2
effective; and (b) the enterprises generating the pollution are economically viable. The
financial appraisal would assess the financial viability of the enterprises and test the debt
service coverage ratio of the enterprises, which should be no less than 1.4 times. The
Bank/IDA would review all subproject appraisal reports in full, including two during
project appraisal, to assure itself of the quality of the appraisal reports submitted.
F. HUBEI ENVIRONMENTAL POLLUTION CONTROL FUND
30.   Proposed Component ($5.0 million). This component would provide loan funds
to finance small-scale, high environmental impact investments in clean technology process
change, supporting the core investments in air and wastewater management. These finds,
together with funds now generated through HEPB-administered pollution levy fees, would
be administered by HEPB, through the segregated accounts and independent operating rules
of HEPCF. The appraisal arrangements for these investments parallel those for the
Industrial Pollution Control component given in the previous paragraph.
G. WATER QUALITY MONITORING AND MANAGEMENT
31.   Proposed Component ($2.9 million). The objective of this component is to
upgrade the facilities and strengthen the management of (a) the Hubei Environmental
Monitoring Center (HEMC); and (b) the Wuhan Environmental Monitoring Center
(WEMC). Specifically, the project will help to improve the facilities of HEMC and WEMC
through upgrading of lighting, heating and airconditioning, doors, windows, flooring,
fumehoods and benches. Laboratory and field equipment, and computer hardware and
software for improved data management, would be procured. There would also be
provision for training and technology transfer.
H. TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE AND TRAINING
32.   Proposed Component ($10.2 million). The component would comprise three
main packages described below, together Nvith an allowance for future project preparation.
Details are set out below in the Technical Assistance and Training Table, showing
estimated local and international person-months and other supporting related inputs. The
scope of work and Draft Terms of Reference (TORs) for the main assignments were
reviewed by the Bank/IDA, and are in the Project File.
Package A: Financial Management Services And Training
33.   Objectives. The objective of Package A, the Financial Management Services and
Training package of the Technical Assistance and Training component is to:
(a)   Strengthen the financial management of HUEP wastewater, solid waste and
nightsoil management, and the related municipal bureaus and divisions.
(b)   Strengthen the overall provincial financial management and policy-making
in Hubei Province.



- 71-                      ANNEX2
34.   Scope of Work. The services to be provided under this assignment are for a
substantial consulting assignment, and would include:
(a)   Provision of accounting systems, management information systems and
training in wastewater, solid waste and nightsoil management operations,
and computer training for accounting staff.
(b)   Wastewater, solid waste and nightsoil management utility pricing.
(c)   Provincial financial management.
Package B: Technical Management Services And Training
35.   Objectives. The objective of Technical Package B of the Technical Assistance and
Training component is to ensure the efficient implementation of HUEP while strengthening
sector institutions.
36.   Scope of Work. The services to be provided under this assignment are for a
substantial consulting assignment and would include:
(a)   Quality assurance training for materials production.
(b)   Assistance to improve products technology.
(c)   Wastewater Treatment Plant operations training.
(d)   Solid Waste Management operations training.
(e)   Construction management and supervision.
(f)   Skills upgrading for planning and analysis of development options.
(g)   Xiangfan Wastewater Pilot Treatment study.
Package C: Environmental Strengthening
37.   Objectives. The objective of Package C of the Technical Assistance and Training
component is to support implementation of the Environmental Improvement Action Plan
(see Annex I1). which seeks to improve environmental quality management, monitoring
and control.
38.   Scope of Work. Two elements of the Environmental Improvement Action Plan
will be supported under this package:
(a)   Research in key environmental control problem areas, including township
and village enterprises; effectiveness of the discharge permit system; and
pollution control technologies for small-scale paper and chemical industries.



- 72 -                     ANNEX2
(b)   Training for provincial, municipal, and county EPB staff. This includes
training at the provincial, national, and international level.
Package D: Other: Future Project Preparation
39.   This would provide for the formulation and preparation of fuiture investment
projects yet unidentified.

ANNEX 6: LAND ACQUISITION AND RESETTLEMENT
Overall Preparation of Resettlement Action Plans
1.    Prior to appraisal, all project cities presented the Bank with resettlement plans for
those project components requiring land acquisition. The appraisal mission requested
additional information on certain aspects of the plans and that information, together with the
original plans, provides the basis for appraisal of resettlement for the project components
requiring resettlement. All project cities-Wuhan, Xiangfan, Yichang, and Huangshi-
have such components, as do several of the enterprises proposed for support under the line
of credit.
2.    The resettlement plans for individual cities and enterprises share many features, due
to the fact that all were developed within the same regulatory framework (described in
Chapter 2 of China: Involuntary Resettlement, Report 11641-CHA). The Bank review of
Chinese resettlement policy showed that basing compensation on collective land ownership
(for rural communities) or enterprises (in urban areas) effectively protected the interests of
all groups but the unregistered population (migrants who have not been given the right of
permnanent abode). The preparation of resettlement plans in this project was done with
special attention to possible impacts on members of the unregistered population. Several
such people have been identified as affected by resettlement, and appropriate measures
taken to indemnify them, as explained in the text.
3.    In each city (including cities in which project-assisted enterprises are sited), the
resettlement efforts will be executed by the city land administration bureau, or another
government agency with special responsibility for resettlement. All project cities have large
ongoing investment programs that involve substantial resettlement and the assigned
agencies are therefore experienced in this work. The executing agencies are those typically
used in resettlement work and acknowledged in the Bank's resettlement review to be well
placed to execute the work. Each will be required to submit quarterly reports on their
efforts under the Bank project. The project offices in each city, together with the provincial
project office, shall be responsible for ongoing monitoring of the resettlement effort. In
addition, an independent agency will be retained to evaluate resettlement performance at
regular intervals during active resettlement and 12 months after the last resettlement occurs.
4.    Project components are expected to acquire over 140 hectares (ha) in some 25
discrete sites. This will lead to the permanent relocation of 39 families and temporary
relocation of 137 families. It will also cause some 996 people to be given new jobs on land
within their current company on village, given jobs with new companies, or switch to new
places of self-employment due to loss of cultivated land, fish ponds, or industrial or



- 96 -                           ANNEX6
commercial opportunities. Using the broad Chinese definition of affected people (which
factors in dependents of those losing income streams), a total of some 3,912 people will be
affected by project-induced resettlement. Tables 1, 2 and 3 show the distribution of
resettlement among the project components, resettlement timing and budgets.

- 99 -                      ANNEX6
5.    In addition to the discussions with the provincial project office, preappraisal and
appraisal missions conducted separate discussions and field trips among all subcomponents
in order to understand the basic scope of and preparation for land acquisition and
resettlement. These discussions included project affected people, to validate the findings of
the consultants on the participation process. A brief summary follows of the major mission
and consultant findings. The full resettlement plan, dated November 3, 1995, can be found
in the project files.
Wuhan Wastewater Component
6.    The proposed wastewater component includes the construction or expansion of five
treatment plants and seven pumping stations, together with approximately 90 km of
wastewater conveyors. Sites are scattered around the city, with the largest sites on the
agricultural margins of the urban area. The largest site (Longwanzui) requires acquisition
of 32.6 ha and the pumping station sites the smallest at 0.2 ha each. The wastewater
interceptors will be built along existing drainage canals or under roadways and therefore
require no additional land acquisition. Land taken has been planned to avoid any housing
removal, so all project impacts will be on income alone. An estimated 430 workers and
farmers will need new employment to restore these income streams. The total impact of the
Wuhan wastewater component will therefore be about half of total labor displacement. The
sites of five pumping stations had not been determined at appraisal. Once that is decided,
the needed supplementary resettlement information will be provided to the Bank/IDA.
7.    Because land acquisition will not require any housing removal, communities will
remain physically intact after resettlement. Therefore, if lost income streams can be
replaced through alternative employment in the neighborhood of current employment, the
social and economic fabric of the community will not be threatened by resettlement. The
land to be acquired virtually all falls under collective ownership (the exception being some
pump station land owned by state-owned enterprises). These collective lands are for the
most part controlled by collective-owned companies, in which the affected people are
employees. Land or fish ponds managed outside of such company control are typicallv
under contract to individual households within the village, though in one village such
contracts are also held by non-village (that is, unregistered) workers.
8.    Chinese resettlement compensation strategies are based on the productivitv of the
land acquired, where that productivity is measured in gross unit output value, times a
negotiated multiplier. In practice, both the base productivity figure and the multiplier are
negotiable, and depend in part on the perceived market value of the land. In this project,
agreed compensation averaged Y 1.5 million/ha ($178,000/ha) in Wuhan. Detail-, of
compensation are given in the RAP. The appraisal mission reviewed feasibility ol
compensation in terms of its ability to replace lost income. It did so by comparing the
quantum of compensation to current net income derived from the land. By this measure.
compensation was no less than 20 times net annual income.  At these levels ctf
compensation, risk-free investment in government bonds (which currently pav about
11 percent interest and are inflation-indexed) would yield incomes more than wice lhal



-100 -                      ANNEX6
forgone due to the acquisition. Additionally, labor would be freed to pursue other
productive pursuits. The appraisal mission judged that this compensation level permits
the affected units to meet the goal of fully protecting, or improving, standards of living
after resettlement.
9.    The question remains of how the collective will handle the displaced labor. Details
of their intentions have been given in the RAPs, but the basic strategy is to reemploy people
in other collective enterprises in the village or on other village lands or ponds. This strategy
is riskier than the government bond strategy, but has the advantage of providing
employment rather than simply a long term subsidy and, also potentially higher long term
income streams. It should also be noted that the resettled workers do not face a risk from
this strategy higher than that faced by all members of the affected collective, for the
collective ownership of the assets and employment spreads the risk over all villagers. It
should also be noted that all affected villages have other recent experience of involuntary
resettlement, with which they have successfully coped. They are all being absorbed into
greater urban Wuhan and as growth continues will doubtless lose their agricultural status
altogether. This process is hastened by the current project, but to this time adequate
agricultural land remains to allow those preferring agriculture to continue in that pursuit in
all but one affected village.
10.   In one village, four unregistered households with 16 members had signed a contract
to manage some of the fish ponds that will be lost. Their management contracts stated that
if the ponds were acquired by the state, no compensation would be due. However, the
village has undertaken to reemploy the workers in these families in township enterprises, so
compensation has indeed been rendered.
Wuhan Solid Waste Component
11.   This component will acquire 17.7 ha of land currently employing 176 people. In
this case, the land will be acquired from a state-owned aquatic farming enterprise that has
total holdings of over 4,000 ha of land and employs about 8,000 workers. The displaced
employees were not attached to the land in any contractual sense, but represent the average
employment per hectare across all farm holdings. Of the affected land, 12 ha was used
under loan from the district land administration bureau, which is also claiming
compensation for a permanent transfer of rights to the Environmental Sanitation Bureau. In
the agreement reached, the company will be compensated with Y 1,500,000 ($178,000) per
ha. and redeploy labor as necessary. The affected laborers will therefore experience no
change in status or income.
Huangshi Wastewater Component
12.   The Huangshi wastewvater component will require the construction of three major
wastewater conveyors and a treatment plant outfall pipe totaling some 15 km in length. In
addition, a new wastewater treatment plant with a capacity of 175,000 m3/day will be
constructed. Although interceptors will, for the most part, be laid in the watercourses
currently serving as open sewers and drains, a total of 5 ha of land and fish ponds will need



-101-                       ANNEX6
to be acquired, with two-thirds of this for the treatment plant. No families will lose their
houses to the project, but a total of 3 agricultural workers will need reemployment.
13.   The three agricultural workers needing reemployment had contracted 60 mu of fish
ponds from the Hubin Company, and were said to net some Y 1,800 per mu. The
compensation paid to the Hubin Company for labor resettlement totals Y 600,000, over five
times the net income and adequate to allow risk-free investment to cover all lost income in
place in eight-year bank accounts now yielding 18.64 percent.
Huangshi Solid Waste Component
14.   The provision of a sanitary landfill facility for Huangshi will require the acquisition
of a 12.5 ha parcel of agricultural land in the city suburbs. By acquiring nearly 30 percent
of the village land, the project will displace approximately 61 agricultural laborers who will
need alternative employment. Current agricultural income levels average about Y 2,400
annually. The village will receive some Y 2.5 million to compensate for the lost land and
jobs, or 17 times annual income. Again, a risk-free strategy with total income replacement
is available.  However, using these funds, the village intends to create alternative
employment in village enterprises. The village transport service would employ 5 men and
the construction team 26 men. The village owns catering unit, which will absorb 20 of the
displaced women workers. The remaining 10 women will be offered jobs in village-owned
shops. Wages will average Y 4,800, well above the average farm income level. Any
enterprise-based village resettlement scheme opens the workers to the risk that the
enterprise will not prosper. However, village enterprises essentially cross-insure against
such risk, as workers can be reassigned among them  as conditions warrant.  The
compensation levels are high enough that even enterprises with rates of return below those
of village enterprises as a whole will be able to meet the replacement wage bill.
Vichang Solid Waste Component
15.   The provision of a sanitary landfill facility for Yichang will require the acquisition
of a 24.3 ha parcel of agricultural land in a suburban village, taking about one fifth of total
village cultivated land. Site clearance will require 11 families (with 44 members) to
relocate their housing and 177 affected people will need new employment. The families
needing new housing will be allocated house plots in one of two existing housing clusters
within the boundaries of the existing village. Compensation will be negotiated based on the
principle of maintaining and increasing living standards. Families will make their own
arrangements for new construction and express confidence in maintaining their living
standards.
16.   To facilitate labor resettlement, the environmental sanitation bureau project office
offered one job per affected family in the landfill, with financial compensation to allow the
other family members to reconstruct their livelihoods. However, the affected villagers have
built a successful vegetable growing business, with net incomes about Y 2,400 per year, and
none was willing to become a landfill worker. Therefore, the vi'.lage governmelit hlis
elected to redistribute existing village lands to ensure that all families continue as farmer.



-102 -                      ANNEX6
The Y 4.25 million to be paid to the village (some Y 268,000 per lost job) will be used to
upgrade the existing land and purchase agricultural inputs so that per capita production and
incomes can be maintained on the reduced land base.
Xiangfan Wastewater Component
17.   The proposed wastewater conveyor system and treatment plant for the Fancheng
area of Xiangfan will require the laying of 20 km of wastewater interceptors and conveyors,
a pipe bridge conveying the wastewater to Yuliangzhou, an island in the Han River, a 3 km
long conveyor to a treatment plant and then discharge to the Han. The interceptors and
conveyors will be routed along existing drains and streets in built-up areas. Nonetheless,
construction will compels families to permanently relocate and 137 families to temporarily
relocate during a one month construction period and for new houses to be provided on the
old sites, or original houses restored, at the end of that period. The treatment plant is on an
island prone to flooding before the construction of the Danjiangkou reservoir and the plant
site has no agricultural activity. The acquisition of a 0.06 ha workshop of the Xiangfan Ship
Factory will require relocation of this operation to the main company complex. Acquisition
is not expected to materially affect company operations or employment.
18.   The biggest resettlement challenge in the project is handling the temporary
relocation of the 137 families. The families have all been visited, a census taken, and
resettlement arrangements discussed. The temporary housing, which they expect to occupy
for less than a month will be located close to their present dwellings. In most cases, only a
part of the original house will be affected. In other cases, houses must be torn down during
construction and the construction unit will be responsible for assisting them to rebuild new
housing of at least equal size and quality. During the temporary relocation, their housing
will be provided at no cost, and a relocation allowance will be paid for both moves. The
move itself will be undertaken by the construction company.
19.   The census revealed one family that did not have an urban residence permit. Under
resettlement regulations, they are not eligible for resettlement. However, the city decided to
provide them the same arrangements as all other families. To avoid legitimizing their de
facto residence, the city has listed them not by the farnily name, but as "a family from a
lower government jurisdiction."
Xiangfan Solid Waste Component
20.   The provision of a sanitary landfill facility for Xiangfan will require the acquisition
of a parcel of land in a northern suburban village. Final site selection remains to be made.
Once the selection is confinned, a separate RAP will be prepared and appraised.
Jingmen Cement General Plant Component
21.   This cement plant will relocate to a new, 11.5 ha site in Meiman village of Ziling
town. The site includes the housing of 16 families of 59 people, all of whom will be
resettled within Meiman village at a distance of no more than I km from their current



-103 -                      ANNEX6
housing. The land acquired was used for housing and associated gardening and house-
based activities. Crops were not planted on this land, which is of generally low quality for
agriculture.
22.   The families needing new housing have negotiated compensation based on housing
size and condition, averaging about Y 42,000 per house (the current housing averages just
under 70 m2 per family and is of brick and tile construction). Families will be allocated
house plots of size equal to the current plots, allowing resumption of home garden and other
activities. They will make their own arrangements for new construction and express
confidence in maintaining their living standards.
23.   Aside from the housing situation, just described, the land yielded little cash income.
As a village common land, it produced less than Y 3,750 per ha in income, or Y 43,000
total. Because current farming activities will not be affected, no labor resettlement is
needed. Based on the resettlement regulations, the village has negotiated a payment of
Y 1. I million for lost use of the land, which would yield Y 126,000 in risk-free income.
Yichang City Cement General Plant
24.   This cement plant will relocate to a new site of 11.5 ha in Huangshan village, 15 km
from Yichang. This will require 7 families with 25 members to move their houses and will
take 9.3 ha of cultivated land and fish ponds. The cultivated land take will displace an
estimated 119 workers, all of whom will need new jobs.
25.   As in other villages so affected, each family will be given a new house plot at least
as large as the old and within the existing village. In this village, affected housing has a
wider quality range than in other affected villages, with the best housing being two-story
brick-and-concrete construction and the worst adobe and wood. Compensation averages
just over Y 35,000 per family, with a high of Y 57,000 and low of Y 8,700. Again, as in
other villages, the owners will make their own rebuilding arrangements. The compensation
received is judged adequate by the owners to replace their current housing to an equal or
higher standard.
26.   The cement plant has offered to solve the labor resettlement problem by offering the
villagers staff positions in the new plant. The village will be able to offer residents the
opportunity to continue as farmers or work in the plant. The plant jobs are expected to be in
demand, as they offer much more in income and benefits than the Y 200 a month average in
farming. The village anticipates that most families will seek to keep some members ill
agriculture and place others in the plant, thus minimizing family risks while also enjoying
an increase in income.
Xiangfan City Chemical Plant Component
27.   The phosphate workshop of this plant will be removed to the phosphate rock
minehead, requiring the acquisition of 3 ha of land. That land is currently in agriculture,



-104-                         ANNEX6
and its loss will require the labor resettlement of 30 workers. No housing will be lost to the
project.
28.   To meet labor resettlement needs, 30 workers will be offered jobs in the phosphate
workshop. Average worker income in the Chemical Plant now runs about Y 5,000 per year,
in contrast to the Y 1,000 annual average income in the affected village. Employment in
the plant will therefore result in substantial income gains for the affected people. In
addition to those jobs, the village will be paid Y 1.35 million, which it can use to improve
conditions for those not directly benefiting from new jobs.
Resettlement Supervision
29.   Resettlement supervision under this project depends on a combination of normal
Chinese administrative procedure and project-specific actions. In each city, the Land
Administration Bureau has responsibility for ensuring that resettlement activities proceed
as national and local regulations require. Their supervisory activities most often find
expression through routine audits of affected collectives to see that allocated funds are
properly disbursed. Any grievance action by an affected unit or person will also trigger
special supervision.
30.   This project has two additional mechanisms to guard the interests of resettlers.
The first mechanism requires that project entities report quarterly to the provincial project
office on the progress of resettlement, detailing physical and financial progress in the
resettlement component. Simultaneously, affected collectives and enterprises are also
requested to file quarterly reports on compensation received, physical relocation, and any
issues arising. The provincial project office will review the reports for consistency and
follow-up on any problems identified. The second mechanism is that of formal outside
evaluation of resettlement activities during and subsequent to resettlement. Based on
resettlement schedules, the first evaluation is expected to take place in December 1996.
the second in June 1997, then, based on experience to date, a schedule of further external
evaluation to be defined, with a final evaluation 12 months after the final resettlement
activity.  Resettlement problems identified during either of these two additional
supervisory mechanisms will be handled first through negotiation among affected parties,
then, if that is unsuccessful, through referral to the Land Administration Bureau system
for formnal disposition.
Additional Resettlement Action Plans
31.   Every proposed investment under the Industrial Pollution Control component and
the HEPCF will be evaluated for possible resettlement impacts. If resettlement will occur, a
RAP, acceptable to the Bank/IDA, will be prepared. Likewise, any changes in project
design will be evaluated for resettlement impact and the RAP would be amended, in a
manner acceptable to the Bank/IDA, as necessary to reflect such changes.



-105 -                      ANNEX7
ANNEX 7: ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT SUMMARY
Background
1.   In 1993 the Government of China and the World Bank agreed to prepare a possible
loan for the improvement of the urban environment in four major cities in Hubei Province.
lhe project would provide approximately $160 million to the municipalities of Wuhan,
Xiangfan, Huangshi and Yichang for improvements in wastewater collection and disposal,
nightsoil collection and disposal and urban solid waste collection and disposal. For the
control of industrial pollution, some $30 million would be provided to control both water
and air pollution in highly polluting industries. The project would be an important first
effort to clean up urban lakes and rivers along the middle reaches of the Yangtze as well as
to begin dealing with serious air pollution problems.
2.    The lack of sound environmental management is now at a critical juncture in Hubei
Province as the pace of industrial development continues. Routinely, both domestic and
industrial liquid wastes are discharged into rivers, sewers and lakes untreated. Most of
these water bodies have seriously deteriorated to Class III or IV over the past few years with
several lakes such as East Lake in Wuhan becoming eutrophic and displaying algal blooms
each summer. Biological diversity in these lakes is also narrowing with the succession of
several species of carp and deposition of thick sludge layers on lake bottoms. Water
supplies must be drawn from Class II reaches of the Yangtze away frorn urban centers.
3.    In the realm of solid waste, little or no sanitary landfill practices are used. Most
solid waste is simply dumped along the periphery of cities. There is no treatment of
leachate that enters either surface waters or groundwater. Collection and transfer practices
are generally good but disposal remains a serious issue since the price of land has risen
sharply in urban areas. Modern landfill practices are therefore necessary in order to
maximize use of scarce land areas set aside for disposal. Major investment in all four
project cities for landfills, transfer stations and vehicles is therefore necessary.
4.    The project consists of over two dozen components, all with separate EAs
performed by local design and research institutes. Coordination of these studies was carried
out by HUEPO and a final, overall project EA, dated May, 1995, was prepared by Chinese
Research Academy of Environmental Sciences located in Beijing. Each of the component
EAs was reviewed at a detailed level with the overall EA providing conclusions of each.



-106 -                        ANNEX7
Basic Environmental Strategy
5.    In the area of water quality, Hubei authorities have chosen to apply an interim
environmental strategy that seeks to maximize the potential of the Yangtze River for self-
purification in the short run because of its large flows (23,400 m3/sec). This strategy
basically seeks to improve the quality of lakes and streams by diverting wastewater flows to
the river via large collectors and outfalls. Prior to discharge into the Yangtze, pretreatment
on primary treatment facilities are provided to remove solids and grit but not biological
treatment is planned in the short term for economic reasons. Hubei authorities propose to
go to primary and secondary treatment as additional financing becomes available and
depending on the biological condition of the Yangtze River as these new waste flows are
added.
6.    Sound solid waste management in Hubei Province is severely limited by the scarcity
of landfill capacity. Informal dumps exist at the periphery of most cities that need to be
upgraded to sanitary landfills. The project will establish such landfills in each of the four
cities as an pilot or demonstration so that other landfills can be developed by local
authorities. The strategy is to develop these sites so that more refuse can be disposed of in
the future as waste flows increase with population and general economic conditions.
7.    The strategy associated with the industrial pollution control components is of
reducing air pollution primarily and wastewater discharges secondarily. In project cities, up
to 70 percent of wastewater effluents are from industry discharged into a combined sewer
system or directly into lakes and rivers. The components were selected on the basis of
continued financial viability of the enterprise and the seriousness of air and water pollution
for which they are responsible. The relocation of two cement plant and the modemization
of a steel mill will do much to reduce ambient air quality pollutants such as particulate and
S02 in those respective cities. In addition, a pollution control fund will be established for
small industries and the TVIEs, which contribute a great share of both water and air
contaminants in the Province but which are difficult to control without such financial
means.
Project Components and Responsible Government Agencies
8.    Specific project components that required EAs are given below in Table I and basic
project characteristics and responsible agencies are given in Table 2.
Project Description
Social and Economic Perspectives
9.    The six major cities assisted by the Hubei Urban Environmental Projects play a
major role in the social and economic development of Hubei Province.

10.   Wuhan, the capital of Hubei Province, is one of the most famous historical and
cultural cities in China, and an important hub of communications and commerce.
Currently, the urban population of Wuhan is some 3,507,000, the population density is
4,091 person/km2 with a transient population of 800.000. With the widening of reform,



-108 -                     ANNEX7
Wuhan will continue to be a major center of industry, commerce, trade, finance,
communication, science, technology and information in Central China.
11.   Huangshi, the second major project city is located in the southeast of Hubei
Province, on1 south bank of the middle Yangtze River. It is the second largest city in the
Province. Currently, its urban population stands at 570,000, with a total population of
1,350,000 (including four districts and one county ). Following 40 years of construction,
a comprehensive industrial system is in place, which includes metallurgy, building
materials, machine, electricity, clothing, chemical engineering, textile, coal, medical,
food, light industry, electronics, etc.  With the development of industry, Huangshi
became an important center of commerce and inter-regional trade in Hubei, Jiangxi and
Anhui Provinces.
12.   Xiangfan is also a historical and cultural city with some 2,800 years of history. It
is an important communication hub with an urban population is 584,000.
13.   Yichang is an important industrial city located in the western section of Hubei
Province near Xilingkou of the Three fjord of Yangtze River. It is an important harbor
city on the line of demarcation of the upper and middle Yangtze River. In Yichang, the
number of municipal-owned and state-owned enterprises is 206, where the main
industries include chemical engineering, textiles, metallurgy, building materials,
electricity, paper and light industry, etc. Its current urban population is 380,000.
14.   Jingmen is an important communication hub in Hubei Province with advanced
communications. Additionally, the Han River that passes Jingmen city is rather ideal for
water transport. In the beginning of the 1970s, Jingmen oil refinery, Jingmen Power
Plant, and a Cement Plant were established. The current urban population is 165,600, in
which the nonagricultural population is 116,200.
15.   Ezhou is a developing city in southeast Hubei, located in middle of the Yangtze
River. It is an important component of the economic zone of the middle Yangtze River.
Ezhou City has 13 industrial departments predominated by metallurgy, building
materials, machine textile and food.
16.   Social and economic development, environmental improvements and upgrading
of quality of life are important symbols of the sustainable development in the economy in
Hubei Province.
Urban Wastewater Treatment Components
17.   Urban wastewater treatment components include establishment of wastewater
collection systems, pretreatment and primary treatment in Wuhan, Huangshi, and
Xiangfan. The main targets are to improve the drainage system of the three cities, to treat
the wastewater to a preliminary degree, improve the environmental situation of urban
natural waters and assist with recover of their various functions. Currently, wastewater
flows of the three cities are shown in Table 3 to part of which is flow.

I S.   In each of the cities, there are many sewage disposal points that are unknown and
therefore an exact accounting of flows is impossible. In East Lake in Wuhan, there are 11
discharge points. Streams in Xiangfan City have actually become wastewater channels.
19.   The capacity of urbani sewage treatment is almost nonexistent. Predominantly
sewage of the three cities drained directly to the environment without treatment. It causes
serious impact to waters such as eutrophication in important urban lakes, such as East
Lake, Moshui Lake and Ci Lake. In addition, most of these lakes have major sludge
layers at the bottom, which will make recovery much more difficult.  With the
development of urban society and economy, the amount of urban sewage will increase
year by year.
20.   The proposed sewage collection and treatment projects, according to the urban
construction and development plan, are components of a strategic planning approach of
the three cities and will play an important role in upgrading the sewage collection
treatment capacity of the three cities and improving urban environmental situation and
life quality.
21.   Wastewater Management Projects in Wuhan City. The Wuhan City urban
wastewater management project consists of wastewater collection system in East Lake
and three wastewater treatment plants in Erlangmiao, Shahu and Longwangzui; a
wastewater collection system and wastewater treatment plant in 'Western Hankou; the
wastewater collection system and wastewater treatment plant in Moshui Lake wastewater
discharge area in Hanyang Region. In addition, water exchange engineering in East Lake
of Wuchang and Moshui Lake of Hanyang is also included in the projects.
22.   The purposes of the components are as following: (a) to solve pollution problems
in East Lake to make the water quality meet the need for drinking, tourism, breeding and
cultivation, farm irrigation and entertainment and further to improve ecological
environment of the Lake area; (b) to add wastewater collecting systems in Western
Hankou in order to perfect urban service facilities, to reduce the existing threatening to
the public health and to improve environment in the region; (c) to restore water quality ill
East Lake in order to improve the drinking water quality for more than I million persons
in the region and to enhance the sustainable development of industry and tourism.

23.    Wastewater Collection and Treatment Component in Xiangfan. Wastewater
collection and treatment component in Xiangfan City consists of wastewater interception
engineering in Xiangcheng and wastewater interception engineering in Fancheng. The
project content is interception, collection of existing discharged wastewater and passing
the wastewater into wastewater pretreatment plant in Yuliang (the secondary treatment
plant in the future), and the treated wastewater will be sent into the lower reaches of the
Han River at Xiangfan. The aims are to reduce water pollution of urban areas and water
resource intake areas, to improve the city's overall scenery, to meet the need of public
health and comfort, to ensure long-term economic and social development and
sustainable environment while maintaining rapid industrial development in Xiangfan
City.
24.    Wastewater Collection and Treatment Component in Huangshi.  Ci Lake
water pollution management project in Huangshi City includes a wastewater pipe
network, collection systems and wastewater transporting systems built in the Ci lake area,
and a pretreatment system built in the Chenjiawan area. The aim of the project is to
protect the water quality in the Ci Lake, to improve the ecological environment and urban
facilities in Huangshi city and to raise citizens' life of quality.

and landfills in Wuhan, Huangshi, Xiangfan and Yichang cities.   With continued
