26.      Currently, each city has some capacity to collect and dispose of garbage.  For
example, Wuhan has three landfills (with the treatment capacity of 2,225 tpd). Huangshi
has a landfill (with the treatment capacity of 100 to 120 tpd). Xiangfan has a simple
landfills and Yichang has a hygienic landfill (with the treatment capacity of 250 to
350 tpd). The main problems of solid waste management of the four cities are the
insufficient capacity  of collection, transport and  disposal.   The  current method  ot
collection, transfer and disposal and current practices cause severe impacts to the urban



-112 -                       ANNEX7
environment, especially the uncontrolled piling at some temporary landfill or dispose
sites, and lack of strict quality control.
27.   The proposed solid waste management projects will increase capacity of
collection, transferring and disposal of urban solid wastes, to satisfy the requirements of
sound solid waste management in all four cities.
28.   Solid Waste Management Project in Wuhan. The solid waste management
project in Wuhan City consists of three parts: (a) to add 30 waste transport trucks; (b) to
build seven transfer stations; (c) to build Jinkou Waste Landfill deal with 2,000 tpd with
necessary accessories and facilities.
29.   Solid Waste Management Project in Xiangfan. The solid waste management
project in Xiangfan City is composed of the following new facilities: (a) 25 solid waste
transfer stations; (b) 35 compression transport truck; (c) a sanitary landfill with disposal
capacity 380 tpd, waste transporting truck parking site and working rooms, etc.
30.   Solid Waste Management Project in Yichang. The solid waste management
project in Yichang includes the following new facilities: (a) 10 closed waste-transfer
stations; (b) 67 waste transport trucks; (c) development of Huangjiawan landfill site with
the capacity of 500 tpd.
31.   Solid Waste Management Project in Huangshi. The solid waste management
project in Huangshi consists of (a) 42 waste transport trucks; (b) building 10 small waste
transfer stations; (c) building Xisai waste landfill site with capacity of 150 tpd.
Industrial Pollution Control Components (IPC)
32.   There are six subprojects in the IPC component dealing with the industrial
wastewater treatment and air pollution control in plants and the relocation of heavy
polluting enterprises from urban areas to the planned industrial zones. Five of all the
plants selected in IPC Components (Echeng Iron-Steel Plant, ITubei Pharmacology Plant,
Jingmen Cement Plant, Yichang Cement Plant, Erxi Chemical Plant) are major polluting
enterprises in China, and on the list of state operated 3,000 heavy pollution enterprises by
NEPA. All of the six plants in IPC are state-owned.
33.   The Environmental Integrated Engineering Project in Echeng Iron and Steel.
Echeng Iron & Steel Plant, located in central region of Ezhou City, is a combined iron
steel enterprise with mine, sintering, coking, iron-making, rolling and further processing.
Because of the crowded workshops and backyard equipment, the No. I steel mill does not
have adequate pollution control facilities for both emissions and wastewater discharges.
The industrial dust emission is more than 2,340 tons, accounts for 41 percent of industrial
dust emission, and 23 percent of industrial dust emissions in the central area of Ezhou
City. It is the main reason that the atmospheric quality in central region of Ezhou City is
higher than Class II state environmental standard.



-113 -                      ANNEX7
34.   The industrial wastewater of Echeng Iron-Steel Plant is 4,050 x 104 m3/year,
accounting for 93 percent of whole city in which 3195 x 1 03 m3 is drained to Yanglan
Lake, 75 x 103 m3 is directly drained into Yangtze River annually. The industrial water
utilization of Echeng Iron-Steel Plant is 1,212 x 104 m3/year. Part of the wastewater was
recycled without treatment. The wastewater discharges caused a serious impact on
surface water quality of the Yanglan Lake, the Xingang stream and the Yangtze River at
Ezhou.
35.   The proposed project includes two major parts:
(a)    Steel-making environmental project; three existing electric furnaces and
one existing turning furnace will be discarded, and a 80-ton super-high-
capacity electric furnace will be built connected to refining furnaces and
continuous casting machines. High efficient and stable smoke and dust
eliminating facilities, water treatment facilities and noise controlling
instrument will be built. In addition, a steel-slag automatic treatment
system  will be established, by which steel-slag in the whole plant
including the first plant will be changed into useful material, such as
construction material.
(b)   Industrial wastewater recycling: The cyanic-phenol wastewater produced
by the coking plant will be treated, and then discharged into the Yangtze
River though specific drainage pipelines.  In addition, a wastewater
treatment plant with a capacity of 25,000 t/h will be built with the
wastewater flowing into Mengu channel for recycling.
36.   The environmental management project for the No. 1 Steel mill is the first step of
implementation of a 10-year environment-protection plan in the Echeng Iron-Steel Plant.
The project will reduce 41 percent of the industrial dust and 14 percent of the wastewater.
The implementation of industrial wastewater recycling engineering will recycle
95 percent of the wastewater.
37.   Relocation of Jingmen Cement Plant. At the present time, Jingmen Cement
Plant with production capacity of 176,000 tons per year is located at central region of
Jingmen City, in an urban area of stores, schools and hospitals. The main environmental
problems is the discharge of industrial dust, sulfur dioxide (SO2), nitrous oxide (NOJ) and
carbon monoxide (CO). It significantly affects urban atmospheric quality, and the
health, life and work of local inhabitants. The plant not have enough pollution control
facilities with the limited area in the plant. The environmental monitoring data show that
the plant is the biggest dust source in the city. Because of size limits, relocation is the
best way to eliminate the pollution. According to Urban Environmental Strategies and
Plans of Jingmen City, the Jingmen Cement Plant will be moved from the urban area to
the construction material industry planning region outside the urban center.
38.   The proposed new project at the construction materials industrial zone will have a
cement clinker production line of 600 tpd capacity with the new dry production facility of



-114-                      ANNEX7
low-block 5-grade cyclone preheaters. All the production facilities in the urban area will
be removed, and the old factory site will be sold for use as commercial property. After
project implementation, the atmospheric quality in central urban area of Jingmen City
will be improved. With the relocation of Jingmen Cement Plant, advanced and reliable
dust collection equipment will be employed to reduce emissions.
39.   Hubei Pharmaceutical. Hubei Pharmnaceutical Plant, established in 1963, is a
national enterprise to producing medicines, preparations and medical equipment. The
existing wastewater drainage system of the plant is a combined system, and was set up in
1971. The wastewater of all workshops drains from west to east into a 700 m long
exposed ditch through the Jiaozhi channel via the unexposed ditch into the Han River.
The discharged contamination include conventional pollutants and some organic
pollutants such as nitrobenzene and nitrophenol. There is only a small wastewater
treatment plant with a capacity of 420 m3   day.
40.   The implement of this project will increase the wastewater treatment to
100 percent, and reduce greatly pollutants, especially organic. An industrial wastewater
treatment plant with capacity of 606 x 104 tons per year is proposed. Wastewater will be
treated with active sludge. Sludge will be dehydrated and solidified with gravity
concentrating and vacuum filtering.
41.   With the project, all of the wastewater will be treated. It is anticipated that COD
load and BOD5 load will be reduced per year by 2,900 tons and 1,800 tons, respectively.
The project will greatly contribute to improving the water environment in Xiangfan and
the lower reaches of the Han River.
42.   Relocation of Yichang Cement. At the present, the Yichang Cement Plant is
located in the east of Yichang City. It was established in 1958. The cement production is
220,000 tons/year. The major environmental issues are the emission of industrial dust,
S02, NO, and CO, which significantly affects urban air quality and health, and work of
the inhabitants.  The dust emission of the plant is approximately 2,601 tons/year,
accounting for 61 percent of dust emission in Yichang urban region.
43.   The project proposes to move the existing Yichang Cement Plant into the Huayan
Industrial Zone, which is 8 km east of its original site, and upgrade the cement plant with
a production line of 600 tons/year. Advanced 5-levels suspended preheater reverse kiln
technique with 95 percent reduction of dust emission is proposed. This project not only
reduces the emission of air pollutants, but also improves production quality. The existing
plant site will be changed into commercial use.
44.   Xiangfan Chemical. This plant was built in 1954 and is located in Fanxi
Industrial Zone, where its the main production is paratrisodium  phosphate.  The
wastewater is above-standard, reaching more than 1.0 million tons/year. The pollution
load of industrial wastewater takes fifth place among the biggest water polluting
enterprises of the city. The wastewater contains fluorine and high concentrations of
suspended matter passed to the Xiaoqing stream, and finally into Han River. The urban



-115 -                     ANNEX7
part of 3 km long Xiaoqing stream has become a sewer containing waters from industrial
wastewater and domestic sewage in the Fancheng region.  Because of the serious
pollution of the Xiaoqing stream, the water quality of the Han River in Xiangfan became
worse and a long pollution band along the bank has formed. The wastewater treatment
plan of Xiangfan Chemical Plant is part of the effort to control pollution in Xiaoqing
River and protect the water quality of Han River.
45.   The emission of fluorine gas from the plant is more than 20 million Nm3 annually,
which is deposited in areas near the plant. It has had a great impact to life and health of
more than 20,000 residence and workers nearby.
46.   In the project, HF, SiF4 contained in waste gas will be absorbed with wave-wheel
washing method, and will be neutralized with sodium carbonate into sodium fluoride.
The waste gas will be exhausted to meet emission standards.
47.   Erxi Chemical.  Hubei Erxi Chemical Plant is a comprehensive chemical
enterprise, located 50 km from Xiangfan City. It is a key factory in the chemical sector
with main production of synthetic ammonia, ammonium nitrate, concentrated nitric acid,
high-purity methanol, formaldehyde, sodium nitrate and sodium nitrite, etc. The main
pollutants are nitric acid , NOx in air, and COD, suspended matters, ammonia, CN and
oils in water.
48.   The pollution control project of Erxi Chemical Plant is a combined clean
production with end-pipe treatment. The proposed pollution control components include
industrial wastewater treatment, charcoal recovery and waste gas treatment. Post-project,
charcoal can be recovered to 600 tons/year, nitrate can be recovered to 5,000 tons/year,
and SS will be reduced by 800 tons/year, COD 750 tons/year, amino-nitrogen 220 tons/
year, respectively.
Baseline Conditions
Geographical Characteristics
49.   Hubei Province is located in the middle part of China and to the south of
Dongting Lake, which is in middle reaches of the Yangtze River. It extends across
108007'- 116021'E and 29025'-3320'N and covers 710km from east to west and
470 km from north to south. It is adjacent to Anhui province in the east, Jiangxi and
Hunan province in the south, Sichuan province in the west, Shanxi province in the
northwest and Henan province in the north. The province covers an area of 185,900 km2,
which occupies 1.94 percent of the country's area and is the sixteenth largest province in
China. The mountainous area is occupies 56 percent of the province's area; the hilly land
is 24 percent and plain and water area occupies 20 percent of the area.
50.   Wuhan City is the capital of Hubei Province which is in the east. The Yangtze
River flows into the Province from the southwest while the Han River from the west.
The city is divided into three parts by the Yangtze and Han Rivers, i.e., Wuchang,



-116 -                      ANNEX7
Hankou and Hanyang. Wuhan City, with flat terrain and 2-30 meter above sea level, is
mainly composed of beaches and alluvial plains, part of which is 20 meters below sea
level and is lakes and ponds. The geological structure is from the Silurian System to the
Quatemary. The Quatemary stratum is extensively distributed (occupying 90 percent of
the city's area), which consists of gravel layer in Lower Pleistocene, clay in Middle
Pleistocene, and clay, clayey soil, sandy soil, sand and gravel in Upper Pleistocene and
Complete Pleistocene.
51.   Huangshi City is the second largest city in Hubei Province. It is adjacent to the
Yangtze River in the northeast, Shihuiyao Region in the south and Huangshigang Region
in the north. The main lakes in Huangshi are Ci Lake and Qingshan Lake. The City is
located in the hilly area at the north edge of Mufu Mountain, in which Taipojian Peak,
840 m high, in Dongjiakou of Daye County is the highest peak, while the lowest area is in
the east (11 m at port bottom). The average elevation of Keyuedi is 20 to 59 m
(Huanghai elevation). The land form can be characterized by high in south and north,
low in the middle and with lakes within the area.
52.   Yichang City is located in the west of Hubei province, which is a city in the area
of upstream and middle reaches of the Yangtze River. It is divided into two parts by the
River. The city is located in the hilly area, which is at the boundary between Erxi
mountain area and west edge of Jianghan plain. The geological structure is the settling
zone of Jianghan plain. The surface ground is covered with clay as well as small pebbles.
The city area adjacent to the river is flat with elevation of 35 to 80 m above sea level.
The elevation of the hinterland mountain area is 120 to 300 m.
53.   Xiangfan City is located in the northwest of Hubei Province, which is the
juncture of Hubei, Henan, Sichuan and Shanxi Provinces. It is divided into two parts by
the Han River, i.e., Xiangcheng and Fancheng. The Han River, the biggest branch river
in Hubei province, flows into Xiangfan from the west. The city is located in Han River
Valley plain with flat terrain and average gradient of 1%-3%. The area is inclining from
northwest to southeast. The elevation of the first-stage bench is 65 to 68.5 m and that of
the second-stage bench is usually 66 to 80 m.
54.   Ezhou City is located in the southeast of Hubei province, on the north bank of
Yangtze River and downstream of Wuhan City. The city is located in Binhu Area on the
south bank of the Yangtze River and is in the southeast of Jianghan Plain. There are both
alluvial plain and hilly grounds in the area. The terrain is highler in the southeast and
lower in the northwest and has plain in the middle part. The general elevation is
approximately 28 m for the city.
55.   Jingmen City is located in the middle part of Hubei province and in the Han
River valley. The city is located in the transition zone extended from Jingshan Mountain
(south branch of Qinling Mountain) to Jianghan Plain, which belongs to Ezhong Hilly
Area.



-117 -                     ANNEX7
Meteorology and Climate
56.   The yearly average temperature of the province is 13-18C. The coldest month is
January and the monthly average temperature in winter is 2-4C. The yearly precipitation
is 800 to 1,600 mm that is reducing from south to north. Maximum precipitation of most
areas in one year occurs in the summer, which is 300-700 mm, whereas minimum
precipitation occurs in winter, which is 30-190 mm. Generally speaking, precipitation in
spring is more than that in autumn, but contrary situation occurs in West Hubei. The
yearly precipitation is centralized in May-September, which is greatly affected by
summer wind. The precipitation in these five months covers 60 to 70 percent of the
yearly precipitation.
57.   Calamitous weather is often the case in Hubei province, in which drought, flood,
low temperature and much rain in spring, coldness in autumn and hail are commonly
seen. Drought and flood are the most disastrous. The mostly commonly-seen natural
calamity is drought and frequent drought maybe occur in middle summer and autumn
(July to September) with long period, extensive scope and big influence on crops.
Hydrology and Hydrography
58.   Hubei Province lies in the Yangtze River basin. There are in total 1,193 rivers in
the province with a total length of more than 37,000 km, among which 42 rivers are more
2
than 100 km long. Accumulated water area of rivers is 131,567 km, covering 70 percent
of the total area of the province. Due to the influence of topography, rivers flow from
mountains around to the plain in the middle part and congest into the Yangtze River.
59.   The Yangtze River basin is a typical monsoon climate area.  It has rich
precipitation with average precipitation over years being 1,100 mm. The precipitation of
south river is more than that of north river, while the precipitation from middle reaches to
downstream is more than that from middle reaches to upstream. The precipitation time in
Yangtze River basin is closely related to monsoon. Seventy to 90 percent of yearly
precipitation is centralized from May to October.
60.   The Yangtze River runs from west to east across 26 counties and cities in Hubei
province. It flows in from Pianyuxi in Badong County and out at Binjiang in Huangmei
county, with total length of 1,061 km. The maximum flow rate of Yangtze River is
76,100 m3/s (Hankou hygrometric station and following is the same) and the minimum
flow rate is 2,930 m 3/s, with an average flow rate of 23,400 m 3/s. The yearly average
sand transport is 430 million tons, with the maximum volume of 579 million tons in 1964
and the minimum volume of 150 million tons in 1963. The Yangtze River has rich
hydraulic resources with a total length of 5,400 m from river source to mouth.
61.   The Han River is the biggest branch at the middle reaches of the Yangtze River,
which runs from northwest to southeast. It flows from Baihe County of Shanxi province
and into Yunxi county, which runs across 13 counties and cities and into the Yangtze
River at Wuhan. The length in Hubei Province is 878 km. The yearly maximum flow



-118 -                     ANNEX7
rate is 29,100 m3/s and the minimum flow rate is 172 m3/s, with an average yearly flow
rate of 1,640 m3/s and an average yearly sand transport of 127 million tons. The Han
River basin has relatively rich hydraulic resources with a total flow of 1,964 m in the
main stream.
62.   Hubei province is usually called "province with thousands of lakes." There are
320 lakes at present, with a water area of 220 km2. The adjustable storage of lakes is
above 3 billion m3. In a rich water year they can store more than 15 billion m3, which is
equal to 15.9 percent of surface runoff of the province.
63.   East Lake lies on the south bank of Yangtze River, Wuchang District of Wuhan
City, which is a shallow lake in Jianhan lake group. The accumulated area is 119 km2
and the lake surface area is 30.7 km2 at the yearly water level of 19.5 m. The volume of
the lake is 735.0 x 104 m3 and the average depth is 2.56 m.
64.   Moshui Lake is a small shallow lake in Hanyang District of Wuhan.  Its
2                                2
accumulated water area is 21.9 km  and the lake surface area is 3.35 km  at the yearly
6 3
water level of 19.0 m. The volume is 4.4 x 10 m3.
65.   Nantaizi Lake lies in southwest of Hanvang District. The average water area is
5.3 km2 and the average volume is 200 x 10 m . Nantaizi Lake, Sanjiao Lake and
Houguan Lake comprise Dong Lake in Hanyang county (now called Caidian region).
The main rain receiving area is 360 kmn and all lakes are connected with one another in
case of flood . Nantaizi Lake is connected with Yangtze River through the Dongfeng Gate
and East Lake pump station and flood cannot flow back from Yangtze River in flood
period. Moshui Lake is connected with Nantaizi Lake through artificial channels such as
Sixin port and Jiandi connection port, and the lake water can be discharged into the
Yangtze River through the Dongfeng Gate.
66.   Nanhu Lake is located in south of Wuchang District, with surface area of 5.9 km2.
It is connected with Xunsi River ( branch of Yangtze River ) through a branch channel to
the west of the lake. In winter, lake water is discharged by gravity into the River through
Wutai Gate, but in high-water period it shall be pumped into the River by Tangxun Lake
pump station. The main function of the lake is for storage adjustment and sewage
receiving.
2
67.   Ci Lake lies in the center of Huangshi City with water area of 8.15 km , congested
water area of 62.8 km2 and volume of 1,716 x 104 m3 . The reserving period of water is
200 days. Water will be discharged by gravity as water level of Yangtze River is lower
than that of Chi Lake and discharged by pump when contrary situation occurs.



-119 -                      ANNEX7
Existing Environmental Quality
Water Quality
68.   According to water quality monitoring for the Yangtze River from 1986 to 1990,
the water quality of the Hubei reach of the main stream of the Yangtze River is good in
general, most monitoring indicators at all sections meeting with Class II standard of
surface water, with very low detection rate for volatile phenol, cyanide, arsenide, Cr6+,
pb and Cd, except that few items in some areas exceed the national standard.
69.   The Yangtze River at Wuhan. The reach should meet with Class 11 standards.
In the first two years, DO and NH3-N exceed the standards while in the later three years
organic phenol and colititer exceed the standards. The COD concentration is obviously
higher than that at the upper reaches while the concentration of all the pollutants at the
Gongyegang Section is higher than that at other three sections.
70.   The Yangtze River at Huangshi. The background section at Yangtze River
Gorges has a good water quality with the main pollutant of suspended solids. The water
quality at Xiseshan section is rather good except for the increasing concentration of
volatile phenol (still up to the standard). Affected by the urban sewage, the main
pollutants are suspended solid in the full and normal flow seasons and volatile phenol in
the dry flow seasons. Huajingtun section has the similar situation as Xiseshan section
with somewhat less volatile phenol pollution.
71.   The Han River at Xiangfan. As the second largest river in Hubei Province, the
Han River enters the Province from Shuhekou of Shanxi, flowing through Xunyang,
Xiangfan, Jingzhou and Xiaogan, and finally converges into the Yangtze River. The
average date of the 15 water quality indicators over five years meets with Class II
standards except that NH3-N is 0.16 times greater than the standard in the dry flow season
in 1986. The indicators that instantaneous values exceed the standards are NH3-N, NO2,
BOD5, COD, pH, SS and volatile phenol.
72.   Tributaries of the Han River. The Xiaoqinhe stream is the primary tributary of
the Han River, receiving large quantities of domestic and industrial wastewater, resulting
in serious water pollution. At some river reaches, the concentration of BOD5 exceeds
Class V of national surface water standard while COD, Mn, NH3-N and pH exceed Class
IV standards.
73.   The Huchenghe stream, surrounding the east, south and west of Xiangyang, is an
enclosed water-storage landscape water body. The sewage discharge has resulted in
serious eutrophication, with COD, BOD5, NH3-N, TP exceed the requirement of Class II
standard.
74.   The East Lake. Most of the lake area is of light pollution, exceeding Class III
national standards, with the major pollutants of TN, TP, BOD5, COD, SS, phenol and
coliform.



- 120 -                    ANNEX7
75.   The Moshui Lake. The lake receive 2.6 x 107 m3 of domestic and industrial
wastewater, or 1.76 times of the rain runoff annually. The major pollutants in this
seriously polluted lake are COD, BOD5, TP and Pollutants in this seriously polluted lake
are COD, BOD5, TP and TN, exceeding Class V of national standard (GB 3838-88).
76.   The Ci Lake. Ci Lake has also a poor water quality with seriously-polluted area
of 2.3 kimn, accounting for 31 percent of the total water coverage. COD, TP and TN far
exceed the national standards, e.g., COD exceeds the standard 1.8-4.8 times, TP with 0.7-
14 times and TN with 2.4-73.2 times.
Air Quality
77.   Atmospheric environment monitoring network in Hubei province was set up in
1982. Up to 1990, 36 monitoring stations were introduced in the network and with total
number of 139 sampling points for atmospheric monitoring, 127 points for urban and 12
points as background. Main items to be monitored include SO2, NO, and TSP (Total
Suspended Particles). Table 6 is the results of monitoring atmospheric environment
quality in 1990 at six cities with which the project is concerned.

the daily average beyond the standard is very high with high uniterm index.
Environmental Impacts
Wastewater Management Projects
80.   The proposed urban wastewater treatment projects mainly aim at wastewater
collection, treatment and discharge.
81.   Major Environmental Issues. The environmental impact of the proposed
projects occurs primary in the construction phase.



-122 -                       ANNEX7
(a)   The construction phase. Impacts as the result of requisition of land and
possible moving of the houses and enterprises in the preparatory stage:
(i)   resettlements activities;
(ii)    dust raised by construction and spoils management;
(iii)    noise and vibration;
(iv)    environmental system change resulted from vegetation destruction;
(v)    potential road and traffic jam from construction traffic;
(vi)    potential groundwater impacts.
(b)   The Operation phase
(i)   treatment and disposal of the wastes, sludge and stenches from
pretreatment plant and pumping stations;
(ii)    noise and vibration from retreatment plant and pumping stations;
(iii)   impact of centralized discharge of wastewater on water bodies (the
Yangtze River and the Han River);
(iv)    impact of centralized discharge of sewage on aquatic organisms
and benthos;
(v)    impact of equipment check discharge and emergency discharges on
receiving water bodies.
Solid Waste Management Projects
82.   Urban solid waste management projects involve three components, i.e., solid
waste collection, transfer and comprehensive treatment/landfill.
(a)    Major environmental problems in collection and transfer
(i)    odors;
(ii)   refuse wastewater;
(iii)    noise.



-123 -                      ANNEX7
(b)   Major environmental problems with disposal
(i)    The land requisition and preparatory phase
a.    Resettlement;
b.    Impact on surrounding residents.
(c)   The construction phase
(i)   structure and composition change of topsoil and destruction of
existing vegetation resulted from the topsoil stripping and
compaction;
(ii)   soil erosion and dust, noise and tail gas from construction;
(iii)    destruction of existing ecological landscape from the change of
land use.
(d)   The operational phase
(i)   dust;
(ii)    odors;
(iii)   traffic;
(iv)    noise;
(v)    leachate leakage.
(e)    Landfill closure phase. When the landfill is full, the site is closed and
ecological recovery performed.  Major environmental problems are:
potential impact of the leaching solution on surface water and
groundwater.
Relocation of Cement Plants
83.   The newly-established production lines of Yichang Cement Plant and Jinmen
Cement Plant are of the same configuration.
84.   Major Environmental Problems.
(a)   The Construction phase
(i)   vegetation destruction from land use or temporary land use;
(ii)    noise and vibration;

Echeng Iron & Steel
85.   The project proposes to tackle the problem of innovation of steel-making capacity,
cleaning and recycling of industrial wastewater, and treatment before discharge into the
Yangtze River of cyanic and phenolic wastewater.

(a)    The Construction phase
(i)    noise, dusts and solid waste from removing the discarded electric

(ii)    vegetation destruction from land use and temporary land use;
(iii)    noise and vibration;

(v)    dusts and tail gases;

(iv)    disposal of sludge in the open drainage ditch.
Review of Alternatives
87.   In the selection of project components and sites, a complex process of review was
undertaken. First, a long list of components were proposed by municipal officials with
the aid of experts consultants. Some 68 components in the four project cities involving
wastewater were initially proposed, of which seven were finally selected. Cleanup of
East Lake in Wuhan was ranked as Number One because some 10 percent of the city's
water supply comes from this highly polluted source. Once projects were selected, a
review of alternatives required a least-cost approach, involving the least disruption, was
proposed.
88.   On the solid waste side, altematives involved a review of landfill sites and transfer
station sites based on financial resources available. Other disposal methods such as
incineration and composting were immediately rejected as being too uncertain in terms of
reliability and high costs. The only reliable disposal option is sanitary landfilling but the
question of picking a site can be complex. The sites selected (Jinkou in Wuhan for
example) were either already being used as a landfill or a dump, or have been studied for
some time by municipal authorities, design institutes and geotechnical consultants.
89.   The selected sites have to have several attributes; cheap land and of sufficient
scale; easily accessible for transport vehicles; away from communities; a stable and
predictable hydrology; adorable geotechnical characteristics such as an impervious
bottom layer; the availability of cover soil; and a suitable discharge point for the leachate.
Each of the project cities had only three or four candidate sites and the most favorable
was clearly evident.
90.   The issue of wastewater collection coupled with pretreatment was one that
required careful study. The concept as pointed out earlier was to clean up Yangtze
tributaries and urban lakes to the detriment of the Yangtze River itself. Again, reasons
for this included the massive scale of flow and the river's large assimilation capacity.



-126 -                      ANNEX7
This capacity can be used in the short term to dispose of large quantities of urban
wastewater while urban lakes recover and funds are sought for primary and secondary
treatment.
91.   Review of alternatives of IPC components was done by the various technical
design institutes based on expected pollution control benefits, effluent and emission
standards and cost. For each IPC component several alternatives were proposed but
generally, the final decision was based on accepted practice in that industry. In the
modernization of industrial facilities whether a new electric arc furnace or a rotary kiln
for cement production, industry experts usually agree on a single approach.
92.   In the Hubei Urban Environment Project, the review of alternatives was a key step
in component selection as well as in determining how those components would be
implemented. Only sensible and proven approaches were suggested. An exceptionally
wide range of alternatives was rejected because tight funds cannot be squandered.
Environmental Management and Monitoring
93.   Management and monitoring of the proposed pollution control facilities will
require the full attention of local ESBs, EPBs and Provincial EPB. Each of the EIAs as
well as the component feasibility studies include detailed management and monitoring
plans. Provincial and national standards exist for emissions, ambient air quality, water
quality and wastewater discharges. These standards will be rigorously applied in every
case.
94.   In the case of sanitary landfills, sampling points must be established at wells,
treatment plant outfalls and at some distance from the facility for air quality monitoring.
Simple checks of COD, pH and BOD can be carried out on a frequent basis by landfill
staff with the assistance of the local EPBs. More complex monitoring and laboratory
analysis for heavy metals and other hard to detect pollutants a provincial laboratory
should be used. Data from these landfills should be routinely passed to the Provincial
ESB and EPB for final analysis.
95.   In the case of the wastewater components, it is vital that the water quality of the
lakes and rivers from which wastes have been diverted are carefully monitored to be sure
that there is no further deterioration. Clearly, water quality on receiving reaches of the
Yangtze should be frequently checked to be sure the either Class II or III be maintained.
Simple checks of BOD, COD, DO and pH should establish the basic condition of the
water body. This sampling and preliminary analysis can be carried out by local EPB
authorities but the data should also be made available to the Provincial EPB for final
analysis and to be able to track the project as a whole.
96.   For the IPC components, it will be up to both environmental staffs of the
enterprise and local EPBs to carry out sampling. Specifically they need to monitor TSP,
SO2, NO, and CO for compliance to standards. In the case of the Echeng Iron and Steel



-127 -                     ANNEX7
facility and in Jingmen and Yichang, it is vital to determine the improvement in urban air
quality over time as a result of the investments.

ANNEX 11: ENVIRONMENTAL IMPROVEMENT
ACTION PLAN
Implementation Goals
1.    The objectives of the proposed Environmental Improvement Action Plan (EIAP)
are to: (a) improve, during the implementation period of HUEP, the effectiveness of
HEPB in applying its pollution control regulations through the pollution discharge permit
system; (b) carry out research in priority areas of pollution control in Hubei; and
(c) implement a com
prehensive training program at all levels in the Province to improve the capacity of staff
involved in environmental protection in the Province.
2.    The~ planned program indicating goals to improve enforcement of the pollution
control levy fees is shown in Table 1 and the annual targets for ensuring industries in the
Province have pollution control permits are shown in Table 2.
Table 1: IMPROVED ENFORCEMENT OF POLLUTION LEVY FEE
Year                       Percentage
1994                          40%
1995                          40%
1996                          45%
1997                          50%"o
1998                          55%
1999                          60%
2000                          65%



- 133 -                    ANNEX 11
Table 2: POLLUTION DISCHARGE PERMIT SYSTEM As A PERCENTAGE
OF ALL INDUSTRIES WITH POLLUTING DISCHARGES

3.    The provincial program to close down or retool high-impact polluters requiring
special financial assistance is determined annually. In the first quarter of each year,
consultations among the provincial EPB, Planning Commission, Finance Bureau, and
other relevant agencies determines target enterprises. In 1994, these totaled 159 and in
1995, 92.
Research Program
4.    The planned research program includes four studies:
(a)   Survey  of Township  and  Village Enterprise  (TVE) Pollution
Discharges: The TVE industrial sector in rural areas is a rapidly growing
and increasingly important part of China's economy. In recent years in
Hubei, water and air pollution from TVEs represented about 2.2 and
11.7 percent, respectively, of the province's total pollution discharges.
Pollution from TVEs, while not large at this time, represents a growing
problem in the province, because most have no pollution control systems.
The proposed survey will assess all TVEs in Hubei. It will include
assessment of the existing economic situation of each enterprise,
production capacity, process technology, waste discharges, pollution
control and management. Some limited data collection will take place
where statistics are not already available. The future potential pollution
from TVEs.  Costs of treating emissions or substitution of cleaner
technology will be determined and a time-kt und :mplementation program
will be established. The Y 1.0 million survev is expected to start l!v tli
end of 1996 and be completed by mid- 1 998.



-134 -                      ANNEX II
(b)   Survey of Discharge Permit System Implementation: The pollution
control discharge  permit system, established  in  1989, is being
implemented in Hubei to reduce air and water pollution in the Province.
To date, about 1,500 industries have applied for a permnit, but only 150
have been issued.  The current implementation program  calls for
95 percent of the industries to be issued permits by the year 2000. This
study/program will serve to promote the pollution control permit system
among industries in Hubei.  It will stress the importance of its
implementation and enforcement, and ensure the collection of the total
levies determined to be assessable. The Y 500,000 survey is expected to
commence in mid-1996 and is to be completed by mid-1997.
(c)    Study of Pollution Control of Fertilizer Industry in Hubei: There are
about 64 nitrogenous and 40 phosphatic fertilizer plants of varying sizes in
Hubei, producing about 900,000 and 550,000 tons, respectively, per year.
Air pollution emissions from fertilizer plants represent about 25 percent of
the total air pollution in urban areas. The proposed study will: (i) assess
the existing production and water/air pollution situation for fertilizer plants
in Hubei; (ii) determine the impact of anticipated future paper production
capacity; (iii) determine pollution control and technology choice that will
bring the industry into compliance with environmental standards;
(iv) estimate the cost of the interventions and (v) set out a multiyear
program to implement the proposed systems. Estimated cost of the study
is Y 500,000. It is expected to commence by the end of 1996 and be
completed by the end of 1997.
(d)   Study of Pollution Control of Pulp and Paper Industry in Hubei:
There are 327 paper mills in lIubei, producing about 500,000 tons per
year, which places Hubei thirteenth in production capacity in China. Only
about 12 percent of the wastewater discharges is treated to standards, and
the remainder is discharged, untreated, to watercourses. The proposed
study will:  (i) assess the existing production and water/air pollution
situation for paper mills in Hubei; (ii) determine the impact of anticipated
future paper production capacity; (iii) determine pollution control and
technology choice that will bring the industry into compliance with
environmental standards; (iv) estimate the cost of the interventions and
(v) set out a multiyear program to implement the proposed systems.
Estimated cost of the study is Y 600,000. It is expected to commence by
mid- 1996 and be completed by mid- 1997.
5.    The research program serves several purposes. The TVE study will help EPB
assess the impact of TVE pollution and adequacy of EPB regulations. Based onI the
study, the provincial EPB will seek any needed regulatory changes. The discharge permnit
study evaluates EPB's most important policv change over the life of the project, and will



-135-                     ANNEXI1
highlight needed adjustments in the policy. The industry pollution control studies will be
implemented in part through HEPCF financing.
Training Program
6.    The training program of the EIAP includes for training at provincial, national and
international levels. It is expected that about 1,000 environmental staff and officials per
year would be involved in some form of training under the EIAP. The total cost of the
training program is estimated to be Y 808,000. The areas of training are indicated below:
(a)   Environmental Planning
(b)   Environmental Statistics
(c)   Environmental Planning
(d)   Registration of Discharges
(e)   Discharge Permit
(f)   21 st Century Agenda
(g)   Environmental Protection Archives
(h)   Environmental Monitoring
(i)   Environmental Products
(j)   Nature Reserves Management Regulation
(k)   Environmental Management of Construction
(I)   Public Clerk System of Environmental Protection Sector



- 136-                      ANNEX 12
ANNEX 12: HUBEI ENVIRONMENTAL POLLUTION
CONTROL FUND
Introduction
1.    China is taking a variety of measures to bring municipal and industrial pollution
under control. One method, addressed to industries, is to create revolving loan funds at the
provincial or municipal level that provide financing for the control of liquid, solid and
gaseous wastes, particularly to those with the greatest environrnental impact. A regulatory
framework wherein industries are required to meet specified waste discharge standards and
an institutional structure to organize and operate the funds are prerequisite to their success.
Almost 4,000 people are engaged in pollution control activities in the province.
2.    In 1982, Chinese environmental law provided for the establishment of provincial.
municipal, and county environmental funds financed by pollution fees. These originally
provided subsidies and grants for pollution reduction investments in industrial and
municipal pollution reduction projects, and for EPB environmental monitoring and
enforcement. In 1988, an amendment allowed up to 30 percent of the fees to be loaned.
rather than granted, to enterprises.  Bank projects in Tianjin, Jiangsu, Liaoning and
Zhejiang, and the Medium-Sized Cities project, have supported improved environmental
fund project identification and management.
Pollution Fee Collection and Use in Hubei Province
3.    In Hubei, municipal and county EPBs collect pollution fees, while the provincial,
municipal and county EPBs jointly plan fee collection and utilization. According to a fund
allocation plan provided by the EPBs, the local finance bureaus issue orders and extend
funds to subprovincial level PCBCs for loan disbursement.
4.    Fees are assessed according to waste discharge information provided to levy offices
by the local monitoring stations. On the average, large polluting industries should be
monitored monthly. However, due to lack of monitoring resources, some industries receive
their fee bill according to waste discharge load estimates by monitoring stations. In Hubei.
the top individual polluters remain the steel industry, cement and chemicals.
5.    Fee rates have been established for wastewater discharges, waste gas emissions,
solid waste dumping and noise pollution. Between 1985 and 1993, total fee collection
amounts to Y 583 million from 5,640 enterprises. Of the collected fees, about 71 percent
were used for industrial pollution control, 4 percent for nonindustrial environmental
improvement projects and 25 percent for EPBs' environmental monitoring and



-137-                       ANNEX 12
eniorcement. During 1985 to 1993, about 7,800 industrial pollution control projects were
supported by pollution fee funds, totaling about Y 1.2 billion, of which 24 percent came
froii El'13 sources. In 1993 alone, some 209 pollution sources were treated. Pollution fees
for indtustrial pollution control clearly played an important role in Hubei.
6.    Bank Experience in China with Environmental Funds. The Bank has supported
the establishment of environmental funds under five different projects and four of them
have been in operation for at least one year. The Bank-assisted funds were found to have
the following advantages over other funds:
(a)   they provide a stronger framework for management, including organization,
staffing and operation regulations, and, indirectly, provide the basis for other
environmental protection management measures including the permit
system and the promotion of pollution prevention programs;
(b)   institute rigorous requirements and procedures for project preparation and
appraisal ensuring a higher project success rate; and
(c)   provide training for capacity-building to staff of the fund offices in the
technical and financial areas.
7.    On the other hand, appraisal procedures have been expensive compared to the size
of the typical loan, which has been under $1.0 million. Due regard needs to be given to
modifications of the appraisal procedures to bring down costs while maintaining quality.
The Hubei Environmental Pollution Control Fund (HEPCF)
8.    The purpose of establishing HEPCF is to strengthen the existing Hubei pollution
prevention program with a technically, institutionally and financially sustainable
mechanism. The Fund would primarily assist small-scale industrial enterprises to control
pollution through waste minimization measures, modifications or renovations to existing
plants to reduce waste outputs or to recycle waste generated during production. Industrial
upgrading projects designed to reduce the amount of pollutant discharge and to save natural
resources and energy, commercial waste recovery services and centralized treatment plants
would also be considered by the Fund. Some 300 small, polluting enterprises that have
been identified as contributing significantly to the provincial pollution load will receive
preferential access to HEPCF.
9.    Organization and Financing of HEPCF. HEPCF would be a self accounting
governrment entity. with initial capital equivalent of Y 87 million. The Bank Loan/ IDA
Credit would provide $5.0 million and HEPB would contribute an equivalent sum from
industrial pollution discharge fees (no less than Y 15.0 million for each of the first three
years). While the size of the Bank/IDA contribution has been kept small ($5 million), the
justification for Bank/IDA support for the fund derives from first, the advantages listed in
paragraphi 6(a) above, second, the elevation of flubei's existing pollution prevention
program into an internationally supported one, supplemented by focused training to further



- 138-                      ANNEX 12
improve environmental management, and third, the confidence building and institutional
strengthening expected to accrue to HEPB.
10.   HPG has designated HEPB to administer HEPCF. HPG would appoint a steering
committee which would oversee the preparation of an operational manual, setting out the
criteria for subloans processing and approvals. The Steering Committee would propose
policies for application for HEPCF funding, formulate rules and regulations for Fund
management, select a depository agency for the Fund and define the terms and conditions
for Fund loans. The HEPCF Steering Committee would also determine institutional
structure and staff composition of the HEPCF Management Office and approve its annual
work plan and budget.
11.   The Fund Management Office (FMO) would have up to 12 staff, to be recruited
over a three-year period, including specialists in environmental science and technology,
industrial processing, economics and finance, and administration. The director would be
appointed by the Steering Committee, and other staff would be locally recruited. The main
role of FMO would be in investment project planning, coordination between borrower and
agent bank, review of project feasibility and supervision of project implementation.
Financial appraisal will be handled within FMO, while technical appraisal will rely on
consultants for industry-specific expertise.
12.   Project Selection. Each application would have to be reviewed by the local
industrial bureau and planning commission, and approved by the concerned local
Environmental Protection Bureau, to ensure consistency with municipal environmental
planning. Based on the general project selection criteria mentioned above, a formula for
ranking would be developed to prioritize submitted project proposals.
Project Management Procedures
13.   HEPCF operating procedures would be drafted and would be approved by the
HEPCF Steering Committee. Fundamental project management procedures would be:
(a)   The Fund Management Office would issue HEPCF directives and
solicitations for project proposals to the sublevel provincial environmental
protection agencies and planning agencies;
(b)   With consent from the local industrial bureau, the enterprise would submit a
loan application to the environmental protection agency and planning
agency of its location;
(c)   The environmental protection agency and planning agency would review the
application for consistency with local development and environmental plans;
(d)   The enterprise would prepare a feasibility study report, including a financial
proposal for investment and an environmental impact assessment;



-139-                       ANNEX12
(e)   After the project has been appraised, FMO would submit the appraisal report
to the World Bank Group for no-objection, along with proposed loan
conditions. The Bank/IDA would provide ex-ante review of the first three
subloan projects and thereafter each subloan of over $300,000, with all other
subloans subject to ex-post review.
(f)   The HEPCFF Steering Committee would be responsible for the final
approval of subloan projects. After approval, FMO would confirm the loan
to the enterprise, any cofinancing agencies and the agent bank;
(g)   FMO would supervise the implementation of the project;
(h)   After satisfying itself as to the quality of a commissioned project, the
relevant bureau would issue a Certificate of Examination and Acceptance to
the enterprise;
(i)    The bureau in charge would submit examination and acceptance documents
for the project to FMO;
(j)   FMO  would separately assess whether the project meets the design
document requirements. If it does not, FMO would arrange for appropriate
departments to intervene, seeking necessary amendments to the project.
Project Appraisal
14.   For the technical appraisal of individual projects, the general criteria to be
considered are: (a) the project's impact on the ambient environment; (b) investment and
operating cost per unit pollution load reduction; (c) efforts made on pollution prevention;
(d) compliance with environmental regulations and standards; and (e) technical feasibilitv
and least-cost option.
15.   The economic appraisal for investment of the individual enterprise must show the
enterprise is economically viable.
16.   For the financial appraisal of the subproject, each enterprise would have to show
that it, as a whole, would be financially viable, including meeting a debt service ratio larger
than 1.4. For joint waste treatment facilities, a financing plan for the operation and
maintenance of the facility would be required.
Project Financing Procedures Between Agent Bank and Borrower
17.   The agent would be a bank acceptable to the World Bank. Once a subloan
application is approved by HEPCF, the agent would execute the loan according to
procedures described below:



-140-                      ANNEX 12
(a)   The agent would confirm the project financing plan with the borrower, in
accordance with the loan agreement signed between HEPCF and the
enterprise.
(b)   The project unit would open an account with the agent.
(c)   The agent would disburse funds upon receipt of a statement of expenditure,
in the form of invoice or letter of credit. Normally, disbursement would be
made once a month.
(d)   The agent would supervise the fund's use by the project unit. If project
funds are found to have been used for any purpose other than the approved
project, the agent would refuse further disbursement and notify the FMO.
(e)   The agent would report to HEPCF quarterly on the financial status of loans
made to borrowers. The agent would also report emerging issues and make
suggestions for improvement as needed.
(f)    At project completion the agent would finalize the financial accounting.
(g)   If projects fail to meet project date or design criteria, the agent shall notify
FMO.
(h)   The agent would assist HEPCF in the collection of loan principal, interest,
late payment penalties and fines.
18.   Disbursement would be made through the agent from the special account for
HEPCF in the Hubei Finance Bureau. The Fund would be audited annually, to include a
management letter.
Loans
19.   The HEPCF loan for any project would be limited to 100 percent of foreign
exchange costs, or 50 percent of total project costs (excluding land), whichever is higher.
Total project size would normally not exceed $1 million. Loan maturity would be three to
five years, with up to two years' grace. HEPCF would bear the subloan credit risk and the
enterprise the foreign exchange risk. The subloan interest rate would be no less than the
IBRD standard variable rate plus a spread of 1.5 percent, with a commitment charge of
0.75 percent. Repayments to HEPCF would be recycled for additional subprojects to the
extent funds are not needed for repayment of the World Bank loan.
HEPCF Project Pipeline
20.   A tentative subloan project pipeline has been prepared by HEPB (see HUEPO
Feasibility Study for details).



-141-                       ANNEX 12
Institutional Development and Equipment Needs
21.   The Fund Management Office personnel would undergo an extensive training
program.  Training courses would include economic and financial analysis, waste
management, waste reduction technology, particularly resource recovery/recycling and
clean technology. Training and equipment for HEPCF will be partially financed under
Package C of the technical assistance schedule.



-142 -                      ANNEX 13
ANNEX 13: FINANCIAL ANALYSIS ASSUMPTIONS
WASTEWATER AGENCIES
1.    Assumptions to the projections of the main financial statements of the Huangshi,
Wuhan and Xiangfan Wastewater agencies for the period 1995-2002 are provided below.
2.    Inflation and Exchange Rates. Yearly general domestic inflation rates used in the
projections are 14.0 percent for 1995, 10.6 percent in 1996, 8.5 percent in 1997, 7.0 percent
in 1998, 6.5 percent in 1999 and 6.2 percent in 2000-02. Foreign price increases are
estimated at 2.6 percent for each of years 1995-2002. The exchange rate used to convert
foreign costs to local currency, where applicable, was Y 8.4 per $1.0. It is assumed that
exchange rate adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power parity over the
projection period.
Income Statement
3.    Sales. Projections of sewerage quantities are based on "minimum demand" and
maximum capacity figures, and at the equivalent of 80 percent of water bills.
4.    Average Tariffs. The average prices in Yuan per m  in current terms are as
follows:
1996    1997    1998    1999    2000    2001    2002
Huangshi      0.18    0.20    0.22    0.24    0.26    0.31    0.32
Wuhan         0.18    0.20    0.22    0.24    0.26    0.28    0.30
Xiangfan      0.18    0.20    0.22    0.24    0.26    0.36    0.36
5.    Operating Costs. Salaries, wages and staff benefits are assumed to increase at the
rates given in para. 2 above. Personnel numbers are assumed to increase by 5 percent a year
after project flows commence. Energy, materials and other costs are assumed to increase in
line with general inflation also. For both existing assets and assets to be constructed under
the project, 1.2 percent of their value is assumed to be expended repairs and maintenance.
Composite depreciation rates have been used to depreciate assets on the basis of historical
cost. The following rates have been used: Huangshi-4.3 percent; Wuhan-4.5 percent;



-143 -                       ANNEX 13
and Xiangfan-3.2 percent The agencies have been exempted from paying business and
income taxes.
6.    Interest and Amortization Expenses. The proceeds of the IBRD loan/IDA credit
are assumed to be onlent to the Huangshi, Wuhan and Xiangfan wastewater agencies by
their respective Municipal Govemments at the IBRD's standard variable interest rate
(which was 7.07 percent per year at the time of negotiations), and 0.75 percent per year
commitment charge over 15 years, including 5 years of grace. Interest is paid annually.
Amortization of loans would be on the basis of equal payments of principal. The
wastewater agencies would bear the foreign exchange risk. The municipalities would
provide the local capital counterpart funds as capital grants.
Balance Sheet
7.    Inventories.  Inventories are assumed to be four months of chemicals and
maintenance materials, and have been projected to take into account general inflation as
well as any expanded levels of operations and construction.
8.    Accounts Receivable. Accounts receivable are assumed to be 60 days of billings
from 1996.
9.    Bad Debts. Bad debts are assumed to be 0.5 percent of billings.
10.   Accounts Payable. Accounts payable are assumed to be two months of chemicals,
utilities and maintenance materials from 1996.
Source and Application of Funds
11.   Working Capital Needs. Working capital needs represent the excess, or otherwise,
of the current year's current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous year's
current assets (net of cash) over current liabilities.
12.   Change in Cash.  Change in cash (which includes short-term  investments)
calculates the balance sheet cash balance for the current year.
